Classification of Ghaya: Isqat and Madd
Definition and classification of ghaya with supporting evidence and dispute resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi classification of ghaya to distinguish between ghayat al-isqat and ghayat al-madd, and justify why the elbows are obligatory in wudu despite the apparent limit of the verse.

Core Idea
The ghaya either drops what is beyond (isqat) or extends up to it (madd); the limit's inclusion depends on the prior clause's scope.

In legal interpretation, the word 'ila' (to/until) often marks a limit. But does the limit itself fall under the ruling? The Hanafi school developed a nuanced classification based on the nature of the preceding clause. This lesson unpacks that classification, its evidence, and its application to key examples like wudu and fasting.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types of ghaya
We classify ghaya into ghayat al-isqat (limit of dropping) and ghayat al-madd (limit of extension). The key is whether the prior clause would have included the limit if the ghaya were absent.
This classification is unique to the Hanafi school, based on induction (istiqra') from the Quran and Sunnah.
2
Identify the condition for each type
For ghayat al-isqat, the prior clause inherently covers the limit; the ghaya only drops what is beyond. For ghayat al-madd, the prior clause does not cover the limit; the ghaya extends the ruling up to it without inclusion.
Example: in 'fast until night' (Quran 2:187), the prior clause 'fast' does not include night, so it is ghayat al-madd; night is not included in the fasting obligation.
3
Analyze the wudu example
The verse says 'wash your hands to the elbows' (Quran 5:6). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, without the Sunnah, the elbows would not be included because the command 'wash your hands' originally applies to the hands; the ghaya is ghayat al-madd. However, the Prophet's practice of washing the elbows is a separate Sunnah evidence that makes them obligatory.
This shows that the ghaya alone does not include the limit; the inclusion must be proven by an independent evidence.
4
Understand the dispute with Qadi Abu Zaid
He objected that there is no prior general ruling to drop, so the classification is invalid. The Hanafi response clarifies that the classification does not posit an existing ruling; it describes what the form of speech would have indicated had the ghaya been absent.
The classification is based on the hypothetical scope of the prior clause, not on an actual ruling that gets dropped.
5
Apply the classification to the option (khiyar) contract
In khiyar, the ghaya is ghayat al-madd because perpetual option is invalid; the contract needs a defined term. Thus, the option period ends at the limit without including it.
This illustrates the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإنه لولاه لتناول وجوب الغسل للمرافق بل لما بعدها، ولذا فهم بعض الصحابة في التيمم اليد كله إلى الإبط، كما حكي في الكشف ناقلاً عن المبسوط (فيدخل) الغاية حينئذ في الحكم لأنه كان داخلاً فلا يخرج (ويسمى) هذا غاية الإسقاط و التفصيل بـ (عدمه) أي عدم تناول الصدر لولا الغاية (كالليل) فإنه لولاه لما دخل في الصوم فإنه إمساك في النهار (فلا) يدخل في الحكم لأنه كان خارجاً فبقي كذلك (ويسمى غاية المد حسن خبر لقوله : والتفصيل (وقد تأيد) هذا التفصيل باتفاق أكثر أئمة الفقه وأجلة اللغة) قال صاحب الكشف ناقلاً عن المبسوط : قال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله : لا تدخل الغاية في مدة الخيار لأنها جعلت غاية والأصل إن الغاية لا تدخل في الصدر إلا بدليل ، ولهذا سميت غاية، لأن الحكم ينتهي إليها، دل عليه الصوم إلى الليل والأكل إلى الفجر، ولهذا لو آجر إلى رمضان أو باع بأجل إلى رمضان أو حلف لا أكلمه إلى رمضان لم يدخل رمضان تحت الجمل لأنه غاية ولا يلزم علينا المرافق فإنها دخلت تحت الجملة، لأن ذلك ثبت بالسنة، فإن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وأزواجه وسلم حين علم الوضوء الذي لا يقبل الله الصلاة إلا به غسل المرافق، هكذا حكى الحاكي الوضوء انتهى ؛ وهذا يدل دلالة واضحة أنهما اختارا عدم الدخول، وأما الأمثلة التي أورداها لعدم الدخول، ففيها الغاية غاية المد إلا مسألة الحلف فإن فيها تفصيلاً، فإن الليل غير داخل في حكم إتمام الصوم ذكر أو لم يذكر، وكذا الفجر في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا﴾ [البقرة: 187] فإن صيغة الأمر لا توجب التكرار فإنه لو لم يذكر الغاية لا يتناول الأمر إياها، وكذا في الإجازة فإنها تمليك المنفعة وهي تصدق بتمليك المنفعة ساعة، وكذا الأجل في ثمن المبيع، لأنه تأخير عن وقت وجوبه وهو يصدق بالتأخير ساعة، فهذه الغايات لمد الأحكام المغياة بها، فلا يلزم من عدم الدخول فيه عدمه في غايات الإسقاطات، ولا يلزم منه أن يدخل في الخيار، فإن الغاية فيه غاية المد عنده لأن الخيار المؤبد غير صحيح، فلا يقيد المطلق عن التقييد بالغاية إلا خيار ساعة غير معينة، فذكر الغاية لمد الخيار إلى تلك المدة، ولذا يفسد العقد بالخيار اتفاقاً فإنه يوجب الجهالة المفضية إلى المنازعة، فلا بد من المد إلى الغاية مطلقاً عندهما وإلى ثلاثة أيام عنده وأما مسألة الحلف فالغاية تدخل فيه في رواية الحسن فلا تصلح حجة هذا واعترض القاضي الإمام أبو زيد على التفصيل بأن الكلام إذا اقترن في آخره غاية أو شرط يتوقف عليه ويستفاد من المجموع الحكم المغيا أو المعلق، فليس ههنا حكم الصدر عاماً فأسقطه الغاية بعدها، أو غير عام فمده إلى الغاية، فلا التفصيل المذكور والحق ما قالاه كيف ومسألة اليمين لازمة على طريق الإمام أبي حنيفة، إذ الاعتماد على رواية الأصل دون رواية الحسن انتهى منقولاً منه في الكشف، والجواب عنه أنه ليس حاصل التفصيل أن هناك حكماً عاماً أو خاصاً مفاداً من أول الكلام ثم الغاية أسقطه أو مده حتى يرد عليه ذلك بل المقصود أن الغاية لو كانت بحيث لو لم يذكر ولفظ بما قبله أفاد شمول الحكم الغاية وما بعدها وسميت هذه الغاية غاية إسقاط لا أن هناك إسقاط حكم موجود، وإن كانت بحيث لو لم يذكر لم يشمل حكم ما قبله لها لم يدخل وتسمى غاية المد، لا أن هناك حكماً ثابتاً امتد بالغاية وليس هذا منافياً لتوقف أول الكلام على الغاية، وحاصل التعليل المذكور أن هيئة الكلام لو لم تذكر الغاية معه اقتضت الشمول فلا تغيره الغاية التي شك في خروجها وتغييرها وكذا في الشق الثاني أن هيئة الكلام بدون ذكر الغاية ما اقتضت الشمول فلا يجعله الغاية مقتضياً بل نقول : إن اقتران الكلام الذي يقتضي الشمول بالغاية يدل على أنها لإسقاط ما وراءها استقراء وكذا اقترانها مع الكلام الذي لا يقتضي الشمول يدل على مد الحكم إليها استقراء ، وأما هي نفسها فبقيت كما كانت، وأما مسألة الحلف، فإن سلمت فالتخلف فيه لعله لقرينة أخرى أو بعرف خاص إن تم، وإذا دريت ما صوّرنا لك وعلمت حقيقة الأمر فاعلم أنه ليس الأمر كما زعم البعض من أن معنى غاية الإسقاط أن متعلق إلى فعل الإسقاط المقدر والمعنى اغسلوا أيديكم مسقطين الغسل إلى المرافق، وكيف يكون هذا التأويل صحيحاً مع أنه لا يخطر بالبال أصلاً، وينبغي لك أن تحمل ما في الكشف أن إلى متعلق باغسلوا لكن المقصود منه إسقاط ما وراءها على ما قلنا، يعني أن إلى وإن كان متعلقاً باغسلوا ويكون هذا غاية للغسل لكن الغاية ربما يجاء بها لإسقاط ما وراءها وهو المقصود، وقد يجاء للمد إلى الغاية، ففي الأول تدخل، وههنا القسم الأول فتدخل، فقد آل إلى التفصيل المذكور، فلا يرد عليه أنه إن أراد أن المقصود منه إسقاط الواجب فما وراء الغاية خارج ليس واجباً حتى يسقط، إنما الواجب غسل اليدين من الأنامل إلى المرافق، وإن أراد إسقاط ما وراءها فما وراء الغاية خارج البتة، لكن لا يلزم منه دخول المرافق، فإن إلى لا يدل على شيء، فالواجب ليس إلا غسل اليدين إلى المرافق، وبقي المرافق على الأصل غير واجبة، وإذ قد دريت صحة التفصيل بتناول الصدر وعدمه تم الفرع من دخول المرافق من غير كلفة وقد وقع ههنا في تتميم الفرع أقوال أخر من دون بناء على التفصيل المذكور منها أن إلى بمعنى مع ويرد عليه أن هذا الإطلاق تجوّز، فلا بد له من باعث وما أورد عليه في «التحرير» من أنه صار المعنى حينئذ اغسلوا أيديكم إلى المناكب المرافق، فإن اليد عبارة عما من الأنامل إلى المناكب فقد أفرد بعض أجزاء اليد عن الحكم، وإفراد بعض الأفراد من العام لا يوجب انتفاء الحكم عما عداه فيلزم وجوب الغسل إلى المناكب هذا خلف فالجواب عنه أن لهذا القائل أن يقول : إن سقوط غسل ما وراء المرافق ليس لإفراده من الحكم بل لأنه ثبت بالنقل المتواتر أنه عليه وآله وأصحابه وأزواجه الصلاة والسلام وأصحابه ومن بعدهم إنما غسلوا في الوضوء اليد إلى المرافق فهذا أسقط ما وراء المرافق وبقي هو داخلاً، ليكون إلى بمعنى مع فافهم ومنها أن وجوب غسل المرافق ضرورة وجوب غسل اليد : إذ لا غسله يتم من دون غسله لتشابك عظمي الذراع والساعد، فغسل الذراع لا يتم من دون غسله وهذا معزو إلى المحيط، وفيه أن هذا موقوف على افتراض مقدمة الفرض وهو افتراض تبعي بمعنى أنه افتراض في الحقيقة لذي المقدمة، وإنما ينسب إليها نسبة بالعرض كما مر، وغسل المرافق ليس من هذا القبيل كما يظهر من كتب الفقه، وما أورد في «التحرير» أنه لم يجب غسل الذراع حتى يجب غسل لازمه، بل الواجب
For if it were not for it, it would necessitate washing of the elbows, rather what is beyond them. Hence some Companions understood in tayammum the entire hand up to the armpit, as narrated in al-Kashshaf quoting from al-Mabsut. (So) the ghaya then enters the ruling because it was included so it does not exit. (And it is called) this ghayat al-isqat, and the detail is by (its absence) i.e., the absence of inclusion of the first part if not for the ghaya, (like the night) for if not for it, it would not enter into fasting, for fasting is abstaining during the daytime. (So) it does not enter into the ruling because it was outside so it remains so. (And it is called ghayat al-madd. Good predicate for his saying: and the detail). (And this detail is supported) by the agreement of most leading jurists and eminent linguists. The author of al-Kashshaf said quoting from al-Mabsut: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, said: The ghaya does not enter into the period of option because it was made a ghaya, and the principle is that the ghaya does not enter into the first part except with evidence. Hence it is called ghaya, because the ruling ends at it. This is evidenced by fasting until night and eating until dawn. For this reason, if one leases until Ramadan, or sells with a term until Ramadan, or swears an oath not to speak to him until Ramadan, Ramadan does not enter under the sentence because it is a ghaya. And the (case of) elbows does not apply against us, for they entered under the sentence because that was established by the Sunnah, for the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, his family, his Companions, and his wives, when he taught the ablution without which Allah does not accept prayer, washed the elbows. Thus the narrator narrated the ablution, end. And this clearly indicates that they chose non-entry. As for the examples they gave for non-entry, in them the ghaya is ghayat al-madd, except the case of the oath, for therein is a detail. For the night is not included in the ruling of completing the fast whether mentioned or not, likewise the dawn in His statement: 'And eat and drink' [2:187], for the imperative form does not require repetition, and if the ghaya were not mentioned, the command would not apply to it. Likewise in lease, for it is a transfer of usufruct, and it is realized by transfer of usufruct for an hour. Likewise the term in the price of a sale, for it is a deferment from the time of obligation, and it is realized by deferment for an hour. These ghayas are for extending the rulings they qualify. So it does not follow from non-entry in them that there is non-entry in ghayas of dropping, nor does it follow that it enters in option, for the ghaya therein is ghayat al-madd according to him, because perpetual option is invalid, so the absolute cannot be restricted by the ghaya except for an hour unspecified. Thus the ghaya was mentioned to extend the option to that period, and hence the contract is spoiled by option unanimously because it leads to uncertainty leading to dispute. So extension to the ghaya is necessary absolutely according to them, and to three days according to him. As for the case of the oath, the ghaya enters in it in the narration of al-Hasan, so it is not a valid proof. This, and Qadi Imam Abu Zaid objected to the detail by saying: When speech is connected at its end by a ghaya or condition on which it depends, the totality gives the qualified or suspended ruling. So there is no general ruling in the first part that the ghaya afterwards drops, nor a specific ruling that it extends. So the detail mentioned is invalid, and the truth is what they said. How? And the oath case is binding according to Imam Abu Hanifa, for reliance is on the original narration, not that of al-Hasan, end quoted from it in al-Kashshaf. The response is that the essence of the detail is not that there is a general or specific ruling derived from the beginning of the speech and then the ghaya drops or extends it, such that the objection applies. Rather, the intent is that if the ghaya is such that if it were not mentioned, and the wording before it would indicate inclusion of the ghaya and what is beyond it, then this ghaya is called ghayat al-isqat, not that there is an existing ruling to drop. And if it is such that if it were not mentioned, it would not include what is before it for it, then it does not enter and is called ghayat al-madd, not that there is an established ruling extended by the ghaya. And this does not contradict that the beginning of speech depends on the ghaya. The essence of the reasoning is that if the form of speech without the ghaya indicated inclusion, then the ghaya does not change it, and similarly in the second part that the form without the ghaya did not indicate inclusion, so the ghaya does not make it inclusive. Rather, we say: The conjunction of speech that indicates inclusion with the ghaya indicates by induction that it is for dropping what is beyond it, and similarly its conjunction with speech that does not indicate inclusion indicates extension to it by induction. As for the ghaya itself, it remains as it was. As for the oath case, if conceded, its violation is perhaps due to another context or a specific custom if established. And when you have understood what we have depicted and know the reality of the matter, know that it is not as some claim that the meaning of ghayat al-isqat is that 'ila' relates to the verb of dropping estimated, and the meaning is 'wash your hands dropping washing to the elbows.' How can this interpretation be correct while it never occurs to the mind at all? You should interpret what is in al-Kashshaf as that 'ila' relates to 'wash' but the intended meaning is dropping what is beyond it, as we said. That is, although 'ila' relates to 'wash' and is a ghaya for washing, the ghaya may come to drop what is beyond it, and that is the intent, and sometimes it comes for extension to the ghaya. In the first, it enters, and here is the first type, so it enters. Thus it leads to the detail mentioned. So there is no objection that if he means dropping the obligatory, then what is beyond the ghaya is not obligatory to be dropped; only washing the hands from the fingertips to the elbows is obligatory. And if he means dropping what is beyond it, what is beyond the ghaya is entirely outside, but this does not necessitate entry of the elbows, for 'ila' does not indicate anything. So the obligation is only washing the hands to the elbows, and the elbows remain on the original principle of not being obligatory. And when you have known the validity of the detail concerning inclusion or non-inclusion of the first part, the branch regarding entry of the elbows is completed without difficulty. And here, in completing the branch, other opinions appear without building on the mentioned detail. Among them is that 'ila' means 'with' [ma'a]. This is objected that such usage is metaphorical, and a cause is needed. And what was objected in al-Tahrir that then the meaning becomes 'wash your hands to the shoulders'? [actually 'elbows']? For the hand is from the fingertips to the shoulders, so some parts of the hand have been isolated from the ruling, and isolating some individuals from the general does not negate the ruling for the rest, so it would necessitate washing to the shoulders, which is contrary. The response is that the proponent can say: The dropping of washing what is beyond the elbows is not due to isolating it from the ruling, but because it is established by mutawatir transmission that he, peace and blessings be upon him, his family, his Companions, and his wives, his Companions and those after them, only washed the hand in ablution up to the elbows. So this dropped what is beyond the elbows, and the elbow remains included, so that 'ila' is in the sense of 'with', so understand. And among them is that washing the elbows is necessary due to the necessity of washing the hand, for washing the hand cannot be completed without washing it because of the intertwining of the bones of the forearm and the upper arm, so washing the forearm cannot be completed without washing it. This is attributed to al-Muhit. Therein it is said that this is dependent on assuming a premise of obligation, which is a subsidiary assumption, meaning it is an assumption in reality for that which has a premise, and it is attributed to it in a secondary manner as previously mentioned. And washing the elbows is not of this kind as appears from books of fiqh. And what was objected in al-Tahrir that the forearm is not obligatory such that its necessary concomitant becomes obligatory; rather the obligatory is [cut off]
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an extended discussion on the nature of the ghaya (limit/terminus) in legal language, particularly whether the limit itself is included in the ruling or not. The Hanafi school distinguishes two types of ghaya: ghayat al-isqat (limit of dropping) and ghayat al-madd (limit of extension). In ghayat al-isqat, the ruling would have included the limit and beyond if the ghaya were not mentioned; the ghaya then drops what is beyond, but the limit remains included. In ghayat al-madd, the ruling originally does not extend to the limit; the ghaya extends the ruling up to it but does not include it. The key example is the wudu verse: 'wash your hands to the elbows.' According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the elbows are included because the Sunnah confirms they are obligatory. But without Sunnah, the ghaya would not include the limit. The text reports that most leading jurists and linguists agree on this distinction. The passage then addresses objections and alternative views, including that 'ila' means 'with' (ma'a) or that the elbows are included by necessity. However, the preferred Hanafi view is that the ghaya does not include the limit unless there is additional evidence. The detailed reasoning shows that the ghaya's function depends on the nature of the prior clause: if the prior clause would have indicated inclusion, the ghaya drops; if not, it extends. This is established by induction from the Quran and Sunnah.

Key Terms
الغاية (al-ghaya): The limit or terminus mentioned after 'ila' (to/until) that marks the end of a legal ruling.
غاية الإسقاط (ghayat al-isqat): A ghaya that drops the ruling beyond the limit, while the limit itself is included because it would have been included without the ghaya.
غاية المد (ghayat al-madd): A ghaya that extends the ruling up to the limit, but the limit itself is not included because it was not included without the ghaya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification, why is the night not included in the fasting verse 'then complete the fast until night' (Quran 2:187)?
A) Because 'until' here is ghayat al-isqat, so the limit (night) is dropped.
B) Because the prior clause 'complete the fast' would not include night without the ghaya, so it is ghayat al-madd.
C) Because night is not a time for fasting due to a separate hadith.
D) Because the word 'night' in the verse actually means 'beginning of night'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of ghaya into isqat and madd, based on the hypothetical scope of the prior clause, resolves apparent contradictions in Quranic rulings and highlights the role of Sunnah in specifying obligations.

The Ruling of the Preposition 'Fī' in Acknowledgement of Usurpation
Linguistic-legal analysis of 'fī' in acknowledgement of usurpation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the container (if movable) is a follower (tābi‘) included in the ruling of the contained, and distinguish it from cases of immovable property or extraction.

Core Idea
The word 'fī' (in) indicates real containment—so saying 'in a handkerchief' implies the handkerchief is also usurped.

This passage from Fawātih al-Raḥamūt dissects the linguistic and legal implications of the preposition 'fī' when used in acknowledgements of usurpation. By examining the real and metaphorical uses of 'fī', the Hanafi jurists derive a clear rule: a movable container is a follower of its contents and is therefore included in the ruling. Understanding this reasoning trains you to spot when a word's literal meaning controls a legal outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the operative word
In the acknowledgement 'I usurped a cloth in a handkerchief', locate the word that indicates relationship between the two items.
The operative word is the preposition 'fī' (في).
2
Determine the literal meaning of 'fī'
The author states that 'fī' is for real containment (ẓarfiyyah ḥaqīqiyyah), both temporal and spatial. This literal meaning governs unless a qarīnah (contextual indicator) diverts it.
Real containment means the container actually holds the contained.
3
Apply the literal meaning
If 'fī' is taken literally, then 'thawban fī mandīl' means the cloth is inside the handkerchief. Usurpation of what is contained can only be achieved by also taking the container, so the handkerchief is included.
Thus both items are considered usurped.
4
Identify the exceptions
Contrast with two cases: (1) 'ghasb al-faras fī al-iṣṭabl' – the stable is immovable and cannot be usurped according to the two shaykhs; (2) 'ghasabtu thawban min mandīl' – 'min' indicates extraction, so only the cloth is owed.
Immovability prevents inclusion; 'min' changes the meaning to removal.
5
State the final Hanafi position
The correct view is that the handkerchief is a follower (tābi‘) of the cloth, and the immediate understanding from usurping the principal in the follower is usurping both.
This principle applies to all movable containers when the real meaning of 'fī' is used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة (في للظرفية حقيقة وهي الزمانية أو المكانية ونحو) الدار في يده مجاز فلزما في) قول المقر : (غصبته ثوباً في منديل لأن الغصب في المنديل إنما يتحقق بغصب المنديل، بخلاف غصب الفرس في الإصطبل ، لأن العقار لا يكون مغصوباً عند الشيخين، وبخلاف غصبت ثوباً من منديل، فإن المتبادر منه الانتزاع وبعد للمناقشة فيه مجال، فالأولى أن المنديل تابع والمتبادر من غصب المتبوع في التابع غصبهما
Issue: (The letter 'fī' is for containment, real, and it is temporal or spatial; and like) 'the house in his hand' is metaphorical; so there is obligation in the statement of the one acknowledging: 'I usurped a cloth in a handkerchief', because usurpation in the handkerchief is only realized by usurping the handkerchief; unlike usurping a horse in a stable, because real estate is not considered usurped according to the two shaykhs; and unlike 'I usurped a cloth from a handkerchief', because the immediate understanding is removal. There is room for discussion later. So the correct view is that the handkerchief is a follower, and the immediate understanding from usurping the principal in the follower is usurping both.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic-legal analysis of the preposition 'fī' (in) in acknowledgement statements. The author explains that 'fī' is primarily for real containment (temporal or spatial). When someone says, 'I usurped a cloth in a handkerchief', the literal meaning implies that the handkerchief is also taken, because usurpation of the contained requires usurping the container. This is contrasted with immovable property (a stable) which cannot be subject to usurpation according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Also, if one says 'from a handkerchief' the immediate meaning is extraction, not inclusion. The Hanafi position is that the container is a follower (tābi‘) and is included in the acknowledgement.

Key Terms
تبع (tābi‘): A follower; an item that is implicitly included when the principal is mentioned in a context requiring inclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone says, 'I usurped a cloth in a handkerchief'?
A) Only the cloth is owed.
B) Both cloth and handkerchief are owed.
C) Only the handkerchief is owed.
D) Nothing is owed because it is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The literal meaning of 'fī' (in) for containment includes the container as a follower, unless the container is immovable or the preposition is 'min' (from).

Interpreting 'Ten in Ten' in Acknowledgements
Explaining why the phrase 'ten in ten' cannot be literal container and the default ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of interpreting ambiguous acknowledgements to determine the binding number in phrases like 'ten in ten'.

Core Idea
Numbers cannot contain numbers, so 'ten in ten' binds only ten unless companionship is intended.

This passage explores a classic usul problem: when someone acknowledges a debt with an ambiguous phrase like 'ten in ten', how many dirhams are binding? The Hanafi school uses the impossibility of literal containment to argue for a default of ten, rejecting both the interpretations of twenty (companionship) and one hundred (multiplication) unless explicitly intended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous phrase and the default ruling
Recognize that 'ten in ten' (عشرة في عشرة) is an acknowledgement of debt. The default Hanafi ruling is that only ten dirhams are binding unless further intention is proven.
This is the position of the majority, excluding Zufar.
2
Explain why literal containment is impossible
The preposition 'fī' usually implies containment, but a number (e.g., 10) cannot be a container for another number. Thus the literal meaning is impossible.
The passage contrasts this with 'cloth in cloth', which is possible.
3
Contrast alternative interpretations
If the speaker intended companionship (i.e., 'ten with ten'), then twenty is binding. If arithmetic multiplication is intended, some (Zufar) say one hundred, but the majority hold that multiplication only increases parts, not the number itself.
The Hanafi response uses the analogy of a poor person: multiplying money in the mind does not make one wealthy.
4
Examine the dispute with Zufar
Zufar and a narration from al-Hasan hold that if the speaker intended the arithmetic convention, one hundred is binding. The passage rejects this because multiplication does not change the underlying number.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
5
Understand the underlying usul principle
The principle is that words are taken literally unless impossible; when literal meaning fails, a metaphorical meaning that avoids contradiction is adopted. Here, the least metaphorical shift is to treat 'in' as redundant, yielding ten.
This exemplifies the Hanafi approach to ambiguous language in legal acknowledgements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) لزم) عشرة في قول المقر (علي عشرة في عشرة لبطلان (الظرفية فإن الدرهم لا يكون ظرفاً فالدرهم آخر، وكذا عدد لعدد آخر، وهذا أولى من الاستدلال بأنه يلزم ظرفية الشيء لنفسه، فإنه إنما يستحيل في المعين، وأما المطلق فلا نحو ثوب في ثوب إلا إن قصد به المعية فعشرون) لازم حينئذ، لأنه قصد المجاز، وفيه تشديد عليه فيصدق قضاء وديانة ( ويشمل) بما إذا أراد) المقر (عرف الحساب فينبغي أن يلزم مائة لأن العشرة المضروبة في عشرة مائة وليس كذلك عندهم حيث قالوا : يلزم عشرة إلا في رواية الحسن، وهو قول زفر رحمه الله، وما أوردوا لبيان ذلك أن الضرب لا يفيد زيادة في المضروب نفسه، وإنما يفيد تكثير الأجزاء، وإلا لكان الفقير غنياً بضرب ما في يده من المال في الألف، بل الألوف، فغاية ما لزم بإرادة عرف الضرب، والحساب صيرورة أجزاء العشرة مائة فلا يلزم المائة الكاملة
And (so) ten is binding in the statement of the one acknowledging: 'Upon me ten in ten' due to the invalidity of containment, for a dirham cannot be a container, so the dirham is another thing, and likewise a number for another number. This is better than arguing that it would necessitate a thing containing itself, for that is impossible only for specific things, but for absolute things it is not, like 'cloth in cloth', unless he intended companionship; then twenty is binding, because he intended a metaphor, and there is difficulty for him, so it is binding both judicially and religiously. And it is problematic if the acknowledging person intended the arithmetic convention, then it should be that one hundred is binding, because ten multiplied by ten is one hundred. But it is not so with them, for they said: Ten is binding except in the narration of al-Hasan, which is the saying of Zufar. And what they presented to explain that is that multiplication does not increase the number itself, but only increases the parts; otherwise, a poor person could become rich by multiplying his money by a thousand, even millions. So the utmost required when intending the convention of multiplication and arithmetic is that the parts of ten become one hundred, so the complete one hundred is not binding.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage addresses the phrase 'upon me ten in ten' in an acknowledgement of debt. The literal meaning of 'fī' (in) as containment is impossible because numbers cannot contain other numbers. The alternative interpretation is either companionship (i.e., ten with ten = twenty) or multiplication (ten times ten = one hundred). The Hanafi position (except Zufar) is that only ten is binding because the phrase is interpreted as 'ten and ten' (companionship) only if that was intended; otherwise, without intention, it defaults to ten. If the person intended the arithmetic convention, the multiplication only changes the parts, not the number itself, so one hundred is not owed; only ten is binding. This is the relied-upon view from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
ظرفية (ẓarfiyya): The quality of being a container; in this context, the preposition 'fī' implying literal containment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, if someone acknowledges 'upon me ten in ten' without further intention, what is binding?
A) One hundred
B) Twenty
C) Ten
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'ten in ten' in acknowledgements binds only ten unless the speaker intended companionship (twenty) or, in the minority view, arithmetic multiplication (one hundred).

Distinction between 'fasted a year' and 'fasted in a year'
Explaining the difference in comprehensiveness between direct object and prepositional phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the linguistic difference between direct object and prepositional constructions and derive its legal implications for vows and acknowledgements.

Core Idea
In Arabic, a direct object implies full coverage; a prepositional phrase implies partial coverage — a difference that changes legal obligations.

A subtle shift in phrasing can radically alter the scope of a legal obligation. The Hanafi school pays close attention to Arabic grammatical structures to determine the extent of an action. This lesson unpacks the difference between saying 'I fasted a year' and 'I fasted in a year', and why the omission or inclusion of the preposition 'fī' matters for fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two phrasings
Focus on the Arabic: 'صمت سنة' (I fasted a year) vs 'صمت في سنة' (I fasted in a year). The first uses a direct object, the second a prepositional phrase.
The verb 'صمت' is transitive requiring an object; with 'في' it becomes intransitive.
2
Recognize the linguistic principle
In Arabic, a direct object is fully affected by the action, implying comprehensiveness (isti‘āb). A prepositional phrase only locates the action within the time frame, not necessarily covering it entirely.
This is a well-known rule in Hanafi usul: the omitted preposition gives full coverage.
3
Analyze the effect on meaning
'صمت سنة' means the fasting occupied the entire year. 'صمت في سنة' means the fasting happened at some point(s) within the year.
The difference is between 'throughout' and 'during'.
4
Apply to legal contexts
In vows (nadhr) and acknowledgements (iqrar), phrasing determines obligation. If one vows 'I will fast a year', every day is required. If one says 'I will fast in a year', only some days are needed.
Hanafi fatwa relies on this distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للفرق) الظاهر (عرفاً ولغة بين صمت سنة وصمت في سنة فيفهم من الأول استيعاب الصيام السنة دون الثاني، وقال البعض في بيانه: إن تقدير في يوجب تعلق الفعل بالظرف بنفسه فيوجب استيعابه، وذكره لا يوجب ذلك كما في الفعل المتعدي والمنتسب بواسطة حرف الجر فتأمل
For the apparent difference (customarily and linguistically) between 'I fasted a year' and 'I fasted in a year'. From the first, comprehension of fasting for the entire year is understood, not from the second. And some said in its explanation: the compounding of 'fī' necessitates that the verb relates to the container by itself, thus necessitating its comprehension, while its mention does not necessitate that, as in the transitive verb related via a preposition. So reflect.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between the direct object construction ('صمت سنة' - I fasted a year) and the prepositional construction ('صمت في سنة' - I fasted in a year). The direct object implies that the fasting covered the entire year (comprehensiveness). The prepositional construction with 'fī' only indicates that the fasting occurred within the year, not throughout. Hanafi scholars note that the omission of the preposition makes the verb directly affect the object, implying full coverage; the inclusion of the preposition makes the action partial.

Key Terms
استيعاب (isti‘āb): Full coverage; the verb covers the entire time or object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between 'I fasted a year' and 'I fasted in a year' according to Hanafi usul?
A) No difference, both mean the same.
B) The first implies fasting the entire year; the second implies fasting only some days within the year.
C) The first implies fasting in the first part; the second in the last part.
D) Both imply full coverage but the first is stronger.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the omission of the preposition 'fī' makes the action comprehensive; its inclusion limits the action to occurrence within the time frame.

The Conditional Particle 'In' and the Property of Khatar al-Wujud
Defining conditional tools and explaining the property of 'risk' for 'in'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the conditional particle 'in' and explain the Hanafi position that the property of being 'at risk of existence' (khaṭar al-wujūd) is specific to 'in', not inherent to all conditions.

Core Idea
The risk of existence is a property of the particle 'in', not of the concept of condition.

This passage introduces the Hanafi analysis of conditional tools, focusing on the letter 'in'. It corrects a common mistake: not every condition must be uncertain. The property of 'risk' (khaṭar) is a special feature of certain particles, not a logical necessity of conditional statements. Understanding this distinction prevents misapplications in suspended talāq and other conditional rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate the particle 'in' in the passage and note that it is a tool of conditional suspension (ta‘līq). The author defines it as a word—either a particle or a noun.
The passage states 'إن للتعليق على ما هو على خطر من الوجود'.
2
Understand the property: risk of existence
The phrase 'خطر الوجود' means the condition is uncertain—it may or may not occur. The passage emphasizes that this is a special property of 'in' and the jussive particles.
3
Nuance from Ibn al-Humam
Ibn al-Humam clarifies that risk is not a necessary attribute of conditionality per se; a condition can be certain (maktu‘) or doubtful. The risk property is a distinctive feature of the particle 'in'.
The text: 'ليس الخطر لازماً لمفهوم الشرط، فإن الشرط قد يكون مقطوعاً وقد يكون مشكوكاً وهذا الخطر من خواص إن'.
4
Apply to an example
Consider a husband's statement: 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced.' Since the condition is absolute non-existence (which is certain only at the end of life), the divorce occurs only at the last moment of the lifetime of one of them.
This illustrates that the risk property of 'in' is preserved here—the conditional event (non-divorce) is uncertain, so the suspension applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(مسائل أدوات التعليق) المراد بالأداة الكلمة لأن بعضها أسماء أيضاً. مسألة: إن للتعليق على ما هو على خطر من الوجود، قال الشيخ ابن الهمام ليس الخطر لازماً لمفهوم الشرط، فإن الشرط قد يكون مقطوعاً وقد يكون مشكوكاً وهذا الخطر من خواص إن، والكلمات الجازمة للمضارع، هذا وكون الكلمات الجازمة غير داخلة إلا على ما على خطر الوجود غیر مشهور بل خلافه مشهور قالوا لا تطلق في قول الزوج (إن لم أطلقك فطالق إلا بآخر أزمان (حياة أحدهما، لأن الشرط ههنا العدم مطلقاً) أي العدم رأساً
(Issues of the tools of conditional suspension): The intended meaning of 'tool' is a word, because some of them are also nouns. Issue: 'In' (if) is for suspension upon something that is at risk of existence. Shaykh Ibn al-Humam said: Risk is not necessary for the concept of condition, for a condition may be certain or doubtful, and this risk is a special property of 'in' and the jussive words for the present tense. This, and the fact that jussive words only enter upon something at risk of existence, is not well-known, rather the opposite is well-known. They said: The wife is not divorced in the husband's statement 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced' except at the last moment of the lifetime of one of them, because the condition here is absolute non-existence, i.e., non-existence entirely.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage opens a new section on the linguistic tools used for conditional suspension (ta‘līq). The author defines 'tool' broadly to include both particles and nouns. The letter 'in' (if) is specifically used to suspend a ruling on an uncertain future event—i.e., something 'at risk of existence'. Ibn al-Humam clarifies that this risk is not inherent in the concept of a condition (since some conditions are certain), but is a specific property of 'in' and other jussive conditional particles. The passage then gives an example: if a husband says 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced', the divorce only occurs at the last moment of life (when it becomes certain that he never divorced her), because the condition is absolute non-existence.

Key Terms
خطر الوجود (khaṭar al-wujūd): The state of being at risk of existence; i.e., uncertain whether it will occur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, all conditions must be uncertain.
B) No, it is a special property of the letter 'in'.
C) It applies only to conditions in divorce.
D) It applies to all conditional particles.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'in' has a special property: it only suspends rulings on events at risk of existence.

The Difference Between 'In' and 'Mata' in Conditional Expressions: Generality of Time
Explaining how 'mata' with negation implies temporal universality, causing immediate divorce upon any silence, unlike 'in'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi treatment of 'in' and 'mata' with negation and apply the rule to conditional divorce and delegation scenarios.

Core Idea
Mata implies temporal universality; 'in' does not. Thus, 'mata lam utalliquk' triggers divorce upon any silence, while 'in lam utalliquk' does not.

In Hanafi usul, conditional particles carry distinct implications for time. The words 'in' (if) and 'mata' (whenever) behave differently when paired with negation. This distinction is critical for understanding how conditional divorces and delegations of divorce operate. This lesson unpacks the rule that 'mata' conveys umum al-azmina (generality of times), causing immediate effect upon the first moment of non-occurrence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle and its negation
Look for 'in' or 'mata' followed by a negated verb (e.g., 'lam utalliquk'). Recognize that 'mata' is a particle of generality of time.
2
Apply the temporal generality rule for 'mata'
Understand that 'mata' indicates that the condition applies at every time. Therefore, the negation 'I do not divorce you' is considered at each instant.
This is the key difference: 'mata' triggers immediate fulfillment upon any moment of non-divorce.
3
Contrast with 'in' which lacks temporal universality
The particle 'in' does not imply generality of time. The negation is continuous but not inherently tied to each moment. Thus, silence alone does not fulfill the condition.
For 'in', the husband's explicit statement of non-divorce or a clear indication is needed.
4
Derive the ruling for conditional divorce
If a husband says 'Mata lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq', divorce occurs at the first moment of silence. If he says 'In lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq', divorce does not occur by mere silence.
This is the practical outcome of the usul rule.
5
Extend to delegation (tafwid)
Apply the same principle: 'Mata shi'ti fa-anti taliq' delegates the power of divorce broadly, not limited to the assembly. 'In shi'ti' restricts the delegation to the assembly.
This shows the wide applicability of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف متى لم أطلقك فأنت طالق فإنه يقع فيه كما سكت العموم الأزمنة في متى فالشرط فيه العدم في أي جزء كان وهذا التقرير مما يتوقف على أن يكون متى داخلاً على محقق الوجود، وأما إذا اشترط في مدخوله الخطر فلا يصح أن يراد بالعدم مطلق العدم المتحقق في كل زمان فإنه كما مر في إن ليس على الخطر، والتقرير الأوفى في أطلقك دخل النفي على مطلق الفعل الغير المقيد بزمان فإن أن لا يدل على أزمان وهذا يقتضي استيعاب النفي ودوامه، فإن الفعل كالنكرة يعم بالنفي وفي متى لم أطلقك يقيد نفي الفعل بزمان، فلا يقتضي الاستيعاب فتدبر ولهذا أي لأجل أن متى لعموم الأزمنة لا يتقيد التفويض بالمجلس في طالق متى شئت لأنه لعموم الأزمنة فلا يبطل بالإعراض في بعض الأزمان دون إن شئت أي يتقيد التفويض في إن شئت بالمجلس لأنه لا يقتضي عموم الأزمنة، بل التفويض بمجرد المشيئة، فإذا أعرضت وفقدت المشيئة في المجلس بطل التفويض
Contrary to 'whenever I do not divorce you, you are divorced' - it occurs by silence because of the generality of times in 'mata', so the condition is non-existence in any part. This explanation depends on 'mata' entering upon something of realized existence. But if its object is conditioned to be on the verge, then it is not valid to intend by non-existence the absolute non-existence realized in every time, for as passed regarding 'in', it is not on the verge. The more adequate explanation is: in 'I do not divorce you', the negation enters upon the absolute verb unrestricted by time, for 'in' does not indicate times, and this necessitates encompassing negation and its continuity, for the verb like an indefinite is generalized by negation. In 'whenever I do not divorce you', the negation of the verb is restricted by time, so it does not necessitate encompassment, so reflect. And because 'mata' is for generality of times, delegation (tafwid) is not restricted to the assembly in 'you are divorced whenever you wish', because it is for generality of times, so it is not invalidated by turning away in some times, unlike 'if you wish' - it is restricted to the assembly because it does not necessitate generality of times, rather delegation is by mere will, so if one turns away and loses the will in the assembly, the delegation is invalidated.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage contrasts the behavior of 'in' and 'mata' when used with negation in conditional divorce. The key point: 'mata' (whenever) conveys generality of time (umum al-azmina). Therefore, if a husband says 'Whenever I do not divorce you, you are divorced,' the divorce occurs at the very first moment of not divorcing (e.g., silence), because negating the verb 'I divorce you' over all times means that in any moment he is not divorcing, the condition is fulfilled. In contrast, 'in lam utalliquk' (if I do not divorce you) with 'in' does not imply temporal universality, so it does not trigger divorce upon mere silence. The author refines the explanation: when negation enters upon the absolute verb (with 'in'), it implies continuity of negation; but with 'mata', the negation is restricted by the time circumscribed by 'mata', so it does not imply universal continuity. The author then applies this to a related issue of delegation (tafwid): if a husband says 'You are divorced whenever you wish,' the delegation is not restricted to the assembly because 'mata' covers all times; if he says 'if you wish,' it is restricted to the assembly because 'in' does not imply time generality.

Key Terms
متى (mata): A conditional particle meaning 'whenever', implying generality of time.
عموم الأزمنة (umum al-azmina): Generality of times; the property of a particle to apply to all times.
التفويض (al-tafwid): Delegation of the power of divorce to the wife, often in marriage contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says: 'Mata lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq' (Whenever I do not divorce you, you are divorced). According to the Hanafi position, when does the divorce occur?
A) Never, because the condition is not on the verge.
B) Only at the last moment of life.
C) Upon any moment of silence or non-divorce.
D) Only if he explicitly states he will not divorce her.

Key Takeaway
Mata implies temporal universality (umum al-azmina), thus its conditional triggers at the first moment of non-occurrence, unlike 'in' which does not.

The Particle 'Idha' as a Conditional: Time Adverb or Pure Particle?
Discusses 'idha' as a conditional particle, its transformation into a pure conditional (harf), and its effect on divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the conditional use of 'idha' and apply it to determine the timing of divorce in a conditional divorce statement.

Core Idea
When 'idha' is used for pure condition, it becomes a particle like 'in', and the condition is absolute non-existence.

This lesson delves into the linguistics of the Arabic particle 'idha' and its legal implications in Hanafi usul. While 'idha' primarily functions as a time adverb, it can transform into a pure conditional particle under specific conditions, affecting rulings such as the timing of conditional divorce. Understanding this transformation is crucial for differentiating between the Hanafi position and that of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Guided Path
1
Identify the default meaning of 'idha'
'Idha' is primarily a time adverb (zarf zaman). It indicates a specific time when something occurs.
This is the starting point for all analysis.
2
Recognize when 'idha' becomes a pure conditional
When 'idha' enters upon something on the verge of existence (doubtful event) for a special reason, it can drop its time meaning and function as a pure conditional particle like 'in'. The author refutes objections that this would make the doubtful similar to real; the special reason does not change reality but allows the word to be used in a conditional sense.
The key is that the word was originally used for confirmed events but is now used for doubted ones.
3
Apply to conditional divorce
In the statement 'idha lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq', if 'idha' becomes like 'in', the condition becomes absolute non-existence of the act (divorce). Since absolute non-existence is not on the verge except at death, the divorce only occurs at death.
This is the author's preferred view.
4
Understand the opposing view and its critique
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that 'idha' retains its time meaning like 'mata', so divorce occurs upon any moment of silence. The author critiques their view: if the husband intended pure condition, his intention contradicts the apparent meaning, and the judge should not accept that intention. The disagreement only matters when no specific intention is present.
Both views are legitimate within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا ظرف زمان ويجيء للشرط محققاً فلا يدخل على ما هو على خطر الوجود إلا لنكتة وحينئذ أي حين مجيئه للشرط فقد يسقط عنها الوقت فتكون حرفاً كان وجعل في التلويح مبنى حرفيته دخوله على ما هو على خطر الوجود، وجعله مقتضى عبارة الإمام فخر الإسلام، ثم أورد عليه بأنه إنما يدخل على مشكوك الوجود لأجل النكتة وهذا ليس بشيء، لأن الدخول وإن كان لنكتة مؤذن بسقوط الوقت وبقائه على معنى الشرط، وإن كان ذلك لنكتة وليس أن النكتة تجعل المشكوك محققاً، بل الغاية أن يجعل بمنزلة المحقق، وتدخل الكلمة التي كانت للتحقيق واستعملت لما شك فيه، ثم إنه لما ثبت استعماله في الشرط المحض وجب أن يكون موضوعاً له، لأن الاسم لا يستعار لمعنى الحرف فتدبر ثم إنه يرد عليه أن الدخول على المحظور يوجب سقوط الوقت ولا الحرفية ألا ترى أن الشيخ ابن الهمام ادعى الدخول على المحظور في متى مع عدم سقوط الوقت، ولعله لهذا لم يجعله الشيخ مبنى الحرفية ولا المصنف، وأما قوله إن كلام فخر الإسلام لا يستدعيه، فمنظور فيه فمن شاء فلينظر في كلامه الشريف فلا يقع في إذا لم أطلقك فطالق حتى يموت أحدهما لأنه لما صار كان وبطل معنى الوقت صار شرطه الذي هو عدم الفعل عدماً مطلقاً خلافاً لهما لظهورها عندهما في الظرف ولا يسقط عنه الوقت كمتى، ففي أي وقت سكت وقع ويرد عليهما أنه لو أراد الشرط المحض بمعنى إن يجب أن لا يصدقه القاضي في هذه النية، لأنه نية خلاف الظاهر اللفظ من مع التخفيف على نفسه مع أنه على ما نوى قضاء بالاتفاق وإنما الخلاف فيما لا نية فيه فتدبر
'Idha' is a time adverb and comes for confirmed condition, so it does not enter upon what is on the verge of existence except for a special reason. And when it comes for condition, sometimes the time meaning may drop and it becomes a particle, like 'in'. In al-Talwih, the basis of its being a particle (hurufiyya) is made its entering upon what is on the verge of existence, and he made that the implication of the expression of Imam Fakhr al-Islam. Then an objection is raised against him: it only enters upon what is of doubtful existence for a special reason, and this is nothing, because the entry, even if for a special reason, indicates dropping of time and remaining on the meaning of condition, even if that is for a special reason. It is not that the special reason makes the doubtful realized; rather the utmost is that it makes it like realized, and the word that was for confirmation is entered and used for what is doubted. Then, since its use in pure condition is established, it must be posited for it, because a noun is not borrowed for the meaning of a particle, so reflect. Then it is objected against him that entry upon what is forbidden (or: the prohibited) necessitates dropping of time and not being a particle. Do you not see that Shaykh Ibn al-Humam claimed entry upon what is forbidden in 'mata' without dropping of time? Perhaps for this reason the Shaykh did not make it a basis for being a particle, nor did the author. As for his saying that the statement of Fakhr al-Islam does not necessitate it, it is subject to reflection; whoever wishes may look into his noble speech. So it does not occur in 'if I do not divorce you, then you are divorced' until one of them dies, because when it became 'in' and the meaning of time became void, its condition became absolute non-existence of the action, contrary to them (the two companions) because according to them it is apparent that it is a time adverb, and time is not dropped from it like 'mata', so in any time he is silent, it occurs. And it is objected against them that if he intended the pure condition, meaning 'in', then the judge must not accept this intention, because it is an intention contrary to the apparent wording, to lighten his burden, while according to what he intended, judicially by consensus. The disagreement is only where there is no intention, so reflect.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage discusses the particle 'idha' and its use as a conditional. The author notes that originally 'idha' is a time adverb (zarf zaman), but when used for condition, it can lose its time meaning and become a pure conditional particle (harf) like 'in'. The author mentions the view from al-Talwih that its status as a harf is based on its entering upon something on the verge of existence, and this is derived from Fakhr al-Islam. An objection is raised: it only enters upon doubtful existence due to a special reason, but the author refutes that the special reason does not make the doubtful real; it just treats it as if real. Then another objection: whether entry upon a prohibited item (mahthur) forces dropping of time. The author points out that Ibn al-Humam claimed that 'mata' can enter upon a prohibited item without dropping time, so the criterion is not settled. The author then gives the ruling: in 'idha lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq', the divorce does not occur until one of them dies, because once 'idha' becomes like 'in', its condition is absolute non-existence, which only becomes uncertain at death. This is contrary to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who maintain that 'idha' retains its time meaning like 'mata', so divorce occurs upon any silence. The author further notes that if the husband intended pure condition (like 'in'), the judge should not accept that intention because it contradicts the apparent meaning (zahir) of the word, which indicates time. However, if there is no intention, there is consensus on the ruling (i.e., the apparent meaning prevails).

Key Terms
إذا (idha): A time adverb (zarf zaman) that can be used as a conditional particle; when used as pure condition, it loses its time meaning and becomes like 'in'.
الظرف (al-zarf): Time adverb; in this context, adverbial usage indicating a specific time.
الحرفية (al-hurufiyya): The state of being a particle (harf), i.e., pure functional word without independent meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's preferred view, when a husband says 'Idha lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq' (If I do not divorce you, you are divorced), when does the divorce occur?
A) Immediately upon the utterance.
B) Upon any moment of silence.
C) Only at the death of one spouse.
D) It never occurs because the condition is impossible.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'idha' can lose its time meaning and become a pure conditional particle like 'in', affecting rulings such as the timing of conditional divorce.

Types of Lam al-Ta’rif and Their Preponderance Order
Defining and ranking types of definite article

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five types of lam al-ta'rif and apply the Hanafi usul criteria to determine their preponderance order.

Core Idea
Lam al-ta'rif has five types; the ranking depends on frequency and contextual clues, not just benefit.

The definite article (lam al-ta'rif) in Arabic is not a single tool—it carries distinct meanings that shape how we interpret the Quran and hadith. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut dissects the five types of lam, establishes which takes priority when multiple interpretations are possible, and critiques a common misconception about benefit-based ranking. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for accurate istinbat (derivation of rulings).

Guided Path
1
Identify the five types
List the five types of lam: external covenant, istighraq (comprehensiveness), genus, mental covenant, and nature. Note each type's function—specifying a particular instance, covering all individuals, referring to the essence, referring to a mentally known individual, or denoting the unrestricted nature.
The author adds a fifth type (nature) to the standard four.
2
Understand the preponderance criteria
Analyze why the author prioritizes external covenant first: it adds new information and is supported by prior mention as a qarina. Then istighraq due to high frequency in sacred texts. Genus is lower because it offers no new benefit. Recognize the debate with rhetoricians who favor genus over istighraq.
The author uses 'tabaddur' (immediate understanding) and frequency as decisive.
3
Evaluate the role of context
Note how the author argues that a contextual clue (qarina) can override the benefit criterion—even if one meaning is more beneficial, the qarina determines which meaning is intended.
This principle is used in resolving homonyms and figurative speech.
4
Resolve the disagreement with Sadr al-Sharia
Compare the classification of mental covenant: Sadr al-Sharia subsumed it under external covenant (as a subdivision), so both are treated together and given precedence over istighraq. The apparent disagreement is terminological, not substantive.
This shows the importance of understanding how different scholars categorize juristic concepts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثالثة في المبادىء اللغوية. اللام للإشارة إلى المعلومية أي معلومية المدخول وأقسامه أربعة معروفة: لام العهد الخارجي الذي فيه الإشارة إلى حصة معينة من المدخول، ولام الاستغراق الذي فيه الإشارة إلى كل فرد منه، ولام الجنس الذي فيه إشارة إلى الجنس، ولام العهد الذهني الذي فيه إشارة إلى فرد ما منه وهذا في المعنى كالنكرة. أقول: الحق أن يخمس، والخامس لام الطبيعة في موضوع الطبيعة الذي فيه الإشارة إلى الطبيعة من حيث الإطلاق مثل قولنا: الإنسان نوع. ثم الراجح العهد الخارجي لإفادته فائدة جديدة، وكون الذكر سابقاً قرينة عليه. ثم الراجح الاستغراق للأكثرية في موارد الاستعمال خصوصاً في استعمال الشارع. ثم الراجح الجنس لعدم إفادته فائدة جديدة معتداً بها. وقيل بالعكس بأن الراجح الجنس على الاستغراق ويعزى إلى علماء المعاني والبيان والاستعمال شاهد بالأول، فهو الأحق بالاعتبار. قال في «التحرير» هذا ليس بمحرر، فإن الترجيح عند احتمال الاثنين باعتبار الأكثرية والأفيدية، ولا شك أن الاستغراق أفيد من العهد. وهذا ليس بمحرر، فإن الاعتبار لكثرة الاستعمال والتبادر، ألا ترى أنهما من علائم الحقيقة، وأيضاً الاعتبار للقرينة ألا ترى أنه بها تترك الحقيقة وإن كانت أفيد، ويترجح بها أحد المشترك، وإن كان الآخر أفيد. وههنا استعمال العهد أكثر، وهو المتبادر، والذكر سابقاً تحقيقاً أو تقديراً أو حكماً قرينة عليه فله الاعتبار، وله التقديم. هذا وظهر من هذا أن اللام حقيقة التعريف والإشارة وهو يعرف المدخول وإن كان مستعملاً في معناه المجازي. ثم المختار عند جماهير مشايخنا بل مشايخ الشافعية والمالكية أيضاً بل والحنبلية أيضاً على ما الظاهر أن المدخول حقيقة في الاستغراق عند مقارنة اللام، كما أنه بدونها للفرد المبهم. وينقل خلاف أهل المعاني فيه، وسيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى تحقيقه. وصدر الشريعة لم يعتبر العهد الذهني المشهور قسماً آخر، بل أخذ الجنس بحيث يشمل المعهود الذهني والمعهود الخارجي المشهور، أعني ما فيه إشارة إلى حصة معينة قسمه قسمين: ما فيه إشارة إلى حصة معينة خارجية مذكورة، وما فيه إشارة إلى حصة معينة ذهنية؛ سمي الأول المعهود الخارجي، والثاني المعهود الذهني؛ فهما قسمان من المعهود الخارجي المشهور. ولذا حكم بتقدم المعهودين الخارجي والذهني على الاستغراق، فبان لك أنه لا خلاف بينه وبين الجمهور بحسب المعنى، إنما التفاوت في الاصطلاح، ولا يجب تطابقه. فسقط ما في التلويح أن الحكم بتقديم المعهود الذهني على الاستغراق مما لم يذهب إليه أحد ولا هو صحيح في نفسه، فإن جهة تقدم العهد على الجنس، إنما هو انتفاء الفائدة في إرادة الجنس والعهد الذهني مما لا فائدة فيه أصلا فإنه معنى كالنكرة فافهم.
The third article on linguistic principles. The lam indicates definiteness, i.e., the definiteness of the governed noun, and its divisions are four well-known: lam of external covenant, which indicates a specific share of the governed noun; lam of comprehensiveness (istighraq), which indicates every individual of it; lam of genus, which indicates the genus; and lam of mental covenant, which indicates some individual from it, and this is in meaning like an indefinite noun. I say: the truth is to make it five, and the fifth is the lam of nature in the subject of nature, which indicates the nature in its unrestricted sense, like our saying: Human is a species. Then the preponderant is the external covenant because it provides a new benefit and because the previous mention is a context clue for it. Then the preponderant is istighraq due to its frequency in usage, especially in the usage of the Lawgiver. Then the preponderant is the genus because it does not provide a new benefit that is considered. And it was said the opposite, i.e., that the genus is preponderant over istighraq, and it is attributed to the scholars of rhetoric and eloquence, but usage testifies to the first, so it is more deserving of consideration. He said in al-Tahrir: This is not accurate, because preponderance when two possibilities exist is based on frequency and benefit, and there is no doubt that istighraq is more beneficial than covenant. But this is not accurate, because consideration is for frequency of usage and immediate understanding; do you not see that both are signs of reality? Also, consideration is for the context clue; do you not see that by it the reality is abandoned even if it is more beneficial, and one of the homonyms is given preponderance even if the other is more beneficial? And here, the usage of covenant is more frequent, and it is the immediate understanding, and the previous mention, either actual, estimated, or legal, is a context clue for it, so it has consideration and precedence. And from this it became clear that the lam is real for definition and indication, and it defines the governed noun even if it is used in its metaphorical meaning. Then the chosen view according to the majority of our scholars, and also the Shafi'is and Malikis, and apparently the Hanbalis, is that the governed noun is real for istighraq when accompanied by the lam, just as without it it is for the vague individual. And a disagreement of the rhetoricians is reported regarding it, and its verification will come if Allah wills. And Sadr al-Sharia did not consider the well-known mental covenant as a separate division, but rather he took the genus in a way that includes the mental covenant and the well-known external covenant, i.e., what indicates a specific share he divided into two: what indicates a specific external mentioned share, and what indicates a specific mental share; he called the first the external covenant and the second the mental covenant; thus they are two divisions of the well-known external covenant. Therefore he ruled that the two covenants (external and mental) take precedence over istighraq. So it became clear that there is no disagreement between him and the majority in meaning, only a difference in terminology, and it is not necessary for them to agree. Thus falls what is in al-Talwih that the ruling of giving precedence to the mental covenant over istighraq is something no one has held, nor is it correct in itself, because the reason for the precedence of covenant over genus is the lack of benefit in intending the genus, and the mental covenant has no benefit at all, for it is meaning like an indefinite noun. So understand.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the types of the definite article (lam al-ta'rif) in Arabic. The author begins by stating that the lam indicates definiteness of its governed noun. He enumerates the four well-known types: 1) lam of external covenant (referring to a specific known entity), 2) lam of istighraq (referring to every individual of the kind), 3) lam of genus (referring to the genus itself), and 4) lam of mental covenant (referring to some individual known in the mind, effectively like an indefinite). The author then argues that a fifth type should be added: lam of nature (referring to the nature in abstract, e.g., 'Human is a species'). Next, he establishes the order of preponderance when multiple interpretations are possible. The external covenant is most preponderant because it provides a new benefit and because the previous mention of the noun serves as a context clue (qarina). Second is istighraq, due to its frequent usage, especially in Islamic legal texts. Third is the genus, as it provides no new benefit. He mentions an opposing view that prefers genus over istighraq, attributed to rhetoricians, but the author supports the first order based on usage. He critiques a statement from al-Tahrir that claimed preponderance should be based solely on benefit, arguing that frequency and immediate understanding (tabaddur) are more critical, as they are signs of the literal meaning. He also emphasizes the role of context clues. The passage then discusses the position of Sadr al-Sharia (author of al-Tawdih), who treated mental covenant as part of external covenant, thus still giving it precedence over istighraq. The author resolves the apparent conflict, showing it is terminological. Finally, he dismisses a criticism from al-Talwih that mental covenant has no benefit, explaining that its precedence lies in the same logic as external covenant.

Key Terms
لام العهد الخارجي (lām al-ʿahd al-khārijī): اللام التي تشير إلى حصة معينة من المدخول معروفة خارجاً
لام الاستغراق (lām al-istighrāq): اللام التي تشير إلى كل فرد من أفراد المدخول
لام الجنس (lām al-jins): اللام التي تشير إلى الجنس دون تعيين فرد
لام العهد الذهني (lām al-ʿahd al-dhihnī): اللام التي تشير إلى فرد ما معهود في الذهن كالنكرة
لام الطبيعة (lām al-ṭabīʿa): اللام التي تشير إلى الطبيعة من حيث الإطلاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, which type of lam is most preponderant when a context clue is present?
A) Lam of istighraq
B) Lam of external covenant
C) Lam of genus
D) Lam of nature

Key Takeaway
The preponderance of lam types depends on frequency, immediate understanding, and contextual clues, not solely on abstract benefit.

Effect of Lam on Plural Nouns and the Rule of Repetition
Analyzing how lam negates plurality and the rule when a noun is repeated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a repeated definite noun refers to the same entity, while a repeated indefinite refers to a different entity, and identify the effect of the definite article 'lam' on plural nouns in the absence of a covenanted group.

Core Idea
Lam on a plural nullifies plurality; a repeated definite is the same entity, but a repeated indefinite is different.

In this passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut, the author explores how the definite article (lam) affects plural nouns when no specific group is intended, and then derives a crucial rule for when a noun is repeated. The Hanafi school uses induction from the Quran and Arabic usage to establish that if a noun is repeated as a definite, it refers to the same thing (emphasis), but if repeated as an indefinite, it refers to something new. This rule is vital for interpreting repeated words in the Quran and hadith correctly.

Guided Path
1
Understand the effect of lam on a plural noun when there is no covenanted group
Analyze the author's claim that lam nullifies the plural meaning. When istighraq is possible, lam indicates every individual; otherwise, it defines the genus. This is derived from induction and textual evidence.
The lam does not preserve the plural; it either gives comprehensiveness or genus definition.
2
Recognize the four divisions of lam and the objection regarding mental covenant
The author addresses an objection from al-Talwih that examples like 'I rode horses' should be mental covenant. Follow the Hanafi response: mental covenant is estimated and does not preserve the plural; lam's property is to negate plurality.
Mental covenant is treated like an indefinite, so it cannot keep the plural meaning.
3
Apply the rule of repetition (hukm al-i'ada) to definite and indefinite nouns
If a noun is repeated as a definite, it is the same entity (priority of covenant). If repeated as an indefinite, it is a different entity (new benefit). This is based on induction and the Quranic verse 94:5-6.
The rule applies regardless of whether the first mention was definite or indefinite.
4
Analyze the dalil from Ibn Abbas and its authenticity
The hadith 'One hardship will not overcome two eases' is cited as supporting the rule, but it is weak. The Hanafi position relies on induction and the principle of 'new benefit' for indefinite repetition, not on this hadith alone.
Knowing the weakness of the hadith prevents over-reliance on it.
5
Critically evaluate the objection and the Hanafi defense
Consider the alternative interpretation that the repeated 'yusr' is for emphasis. The author argues that forcing the meaning to two different eases is strained; the correct interpretation is that the indefinite repetition indicates difference, but the weak hadith shows that the second ease is a new one.
This demonstrates how usul principles guide interpretation of disputed texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا دخل اللام على الجمع ولم يكن هناك جماعة معهودة أبطل اللام معنى الجمعية وأفاد استغراق الآحاد إن أمكن، لأنه الراجح كما تقدم، وإلا أفاد تعريف الجنس سواء تحقق في واحد أو أكثر، وسواء كان مناط الحكم نفسه مع قطع النظر عن الأشخاص كما في الرجال خير من النساء، أو كان مناط الحكم الجنس من حيث تحققه في فرد ما، كما ركبت الخيل ولبست الثياب، فدخل في هذا أمثلة العهد الذهني وسقط ما اعترض به في التلويح من أن مثل ركبت الخيل من قبيل المعهود الذهني الذي فيه الإشارة إلى حصة ما معهودة في الذهن وإذ قد عدّ في المعرف بلام الجنس فأي معنى للمعهود الذهني الذي هو مقدم على الاستغراق وأي شيء هو فافهم والدليل عليه شهادة الاستقراء، فإنه عند عدم إمكان العهد والاستغراق يتبادر الجنس في كلام الله وكلام الفصحاء، وأيضاً استدلوا بأنه لو لم يحمل على الجنس وبقي الجمع فيه على الجمعية لغا حرف العهد أعني اللام وإن حمل على الجنس المقيد بالوحدة لغا الصيغة، فلا بد من الحمل على الجنس فيه ليبقى اللام معمولاً ويكون مدخوله أقرب إلى الجمع، لأنه كما يصدق على الواحد يصدق على الجماعة، واعترض عليه بأنه لم لا يحمل على المعهود الذهني ويشار إلى جماعة ما معهودة في الذهن، فحينئذ يبقى اللام والجمع كلاهما على معنييهما وجوابه أنك قد عرفت أن من خواص اللام أن يبطل الجمعية، فلو أبقى الجمع لنا قطعاً وأيضاً أن العهد الذهني عهد تقديري، وليس معناه حقيقة، ولذا يعامل بالمعهود الذهني معاملة النكرة فلغا قطعاً، والحاصل أن اللام يبطل الجمعية بالاستقراء الغير المكذوب، فلو أبقى الجمع على معناه الجمعي بطل اللام بالكلية ولا يظهر له أثر في تغيير المدخول، ولو غير إلى معنى المفرد بطل الجمعية بالكلية، ويصير مجازاً أبعد، فحمل الجمع على الجنس الشامل للواحد والكثير من قبيل عموم المجاز، وصار المجاز أقرب إلى الحقيقة. هذا والأقسام والأحكام التي ذكرت في اللام بعينها جارية في المضاف إلى المعرفة فقسه عليه. ثم إنه يتفرع على ما عرفت من الترتيب بين الأقسام الأربعة حكم الإعادة، فإذا أعيد المذكور أوّلاً ثانياً معرفة كان عين الأول، سواء كان الأول معرفة أو نكرة، تقديماً للعهد، وإذا أعيد نكرة كان غيره حملاً على الإفادة الجديدة ويشهد لهذا الاستقراء، وما روي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنه موقوفاً ومرفوعاً في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا إِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا﴾ [الشرح: ٥-٦] لن يغلب عسر يسرين لكن لم تصح هذه الرواية عند أهل الحديث، وهو معنى قول الإمام فخر الإسلام، وفيه نظر لا ما وجهوا به أن الظاهر التأكيد والحمل على تغير اليسرين تعسف فإنه ليس يصلح بحال أدنى مسلم أن يجترىء عليه، فما ظنك بقدوتهم؟ هيهات هيهات ما ينسبون إلى من هم متأدبون بآداب الشريعة ولم تتجاوز أقوالهم وأفعالهم عن أتباع السنة . قال صاحب الكشف : إنّ النكرة إذا أعيدت نكرة : كان الثاني غير الأول.
When the lam enters a plural and there is no covenanted group, the lam nullifies the meaning of plurality and conveys comprehensiveness (istighraq) of individuals if possible, because it is preponderant as previously mentioned. Otherwise, it conveys definition of the genus, whether it applies to one or more, and whether the basis of the ruling is the same regardless of individuals, as in 'Men are better than women', or the basis of the ruling is the genus as realized in some individual, as in 'I rode horses' and 'I wore clothes'. Thus examples of mental covenant enter into this, and what was objected in al-Talwih falls, that examples like 'I rode horses' are of the mental covenant type referring to some covenanted share in the mind, and since it is considered defined by lam of genus, what then is the meaning of mental covenant that is preponderant over istighraq? So understand. The proof for it is the testimony of induction, because when covenant and istighraq are not possible, the genus is immediately understood in the speech of Allah and eloquent speakers. Also they argued that if it were not interpreted as genus and the plural remained in its plural meaning, the letter of covenant (the lam) would be void. And if it were interpreted as genus restricted to unity, the plural form would be void. So it must be interpreted as genus so that the lam operates and its governed noun is closer to the plural, because as it applies to one, it applies to many. It was objected: why not interpret it as mental covenant referring to some covenanted group in the mind? Then both lam and plural would retain their meanings. The answer: you already know that one of the properties of lam is to negate the plural, so if we keep the plural, the lam is definitely void. Also, the mental covenant is an estimated covenant, not real, so it is treated like an indefinite, thus it is definitely void. The conclusion is that the lam negates the plural by induction that is not contradicted. If the plural were kept in its plural meaning, the lam would be entirely void and would have no effect in changing the governed noun. If it were changed to a singular meaning, the plurality would be entirely void, becoming a distant metaphor. So interpreting the plural as genus that encompasses one and many is a kind of general metaphor, and this metaphor is closer to reality. And the divisions and rulings mentioned regarding the lam apply identically to the phrase annexed to a definite, so analogize it. Then, based on the ordering of the four divisions, the ruling of repetition (i'ada) branches out: if the mentioned noun is repeated a second time as a definite, it is the same as the first, whether the first was definite or indefinite, giving precedence to the covenant. If it is repeated as an indefinite, it is different, based on providing new information. Induction testifies to this, and what was narrated from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, as a marfu' and mawquf, regarding the verse 'For indeed, with hardship comes ease. Indeed, with hardship comes ease' (Quran 94:5-6): 'One hardship will not overcome two eases,' but this narration is not authentic according to hadith scholars. This is the meaning of Imam Fakhr al-Islam's statement, and there is consideration in it, not as they explained that the apparent meaning is emphasis and interpreting it as a change of the two eases is forced, because it is not acceptable for any Muslim to dare to do so. What do you think of their leader? How far they are from attributing to those who are disciplined with the manners of Sharia and whose sayings and actions did not exceed following the Sunnah. The author of al-Kashf said: when an indefinite is repeated as an indefinite, the second is different from the first.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the definite article, focusing on its effect on plural nouns and the rule when a noun is repeated. The author explains that when lam is prefixed to a plural noun, and there is no specific covenanted group, the lam nullifies the plural meaning. If istighraq (comprehensiveness) is possible, the lam indicates every individual; otherwise, it defines the genus. This genus interpretation applies whether the ruling attaches to the genus itself (e.g., 'Men are better than women') or to the genus as realized in some individual (e.g., 'I rode horses' meaning I rode some horses). The author defends this against an objection from al-Talwih that such examples are actually mental covenant. He argues that mental covenant is not a real covenant and cannot preserve the plural meaning; induction shows that the lam negates the plural. The concept is then extended to any definite phrase: the same rules apply. The second part discusses the rule of repetition (i'ada). If a noun is first mentioned and then repeated as a definite, it refers to the same entity, based on the priority of the covenant lam. If repeated as an indefinite, it refers to a different entity. This is supported by Quranic evidence: the verse 'Indeed, with hardship comes ease. Indeed, with hardship comes ease' (two occurrences of 'yusr' as indefinite nouns). Ibn Abbas reportedly said the first 'yusr' refers to one ease and the second to another, implying that one hardship cannot overcome two eases, but this hadith is weak. The author sides with Fakhr al-Islam's view that the repetition is for emphasis, not to indicate two different eases, as that would be forced. He concludes by quoting al-Kashf that an indefinite repeated as an indefinite refers to a different entity.

Key Terms
حكم الإعادة (ḥukm al-iʿāda): القاعدة: إذا أعيد المذكور معرفة فهو عين الأول، وإن أعيد نكرة فهو غيره
العهد الذهني (al-ʿahd al-dhihnī): إشارة إلى فرد معهود في الذهن، يعامل معاملة النكرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A different entity
B) The same entity
C) It could be either depending on context

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule of repetition: a repeated definite is the same; a repeated indefinite is different, derived from the nature of lam and induction from the Quran and Arabic usage.
