(He argued) for the chosen position (that) it is a meaning intended to be conveyed, and the need to express it is frequent, so it must have been placed for it like other meanings for which words were placed to express them. It was answered that one can dispense, in expressing it, with independent placement (through metaphor and shared word); it is permissible for words to be for specificity and used for generality metaphorically, or to be shared between generality and specificity, then used for generality, so the need for expression is fulfilled and independent placement is not required. (And) it was answered that this is establishing language and placement by opinion and analogy, which has been prohibited. (I say: If it were said in the argument that generality is a rational meaning, the need to express it is frequent, then indication of it is necessary, i.e., there must be some word indicating it, rather many words, otherwise it would be impossible to express and convey generality, and indication has been found through induction in words in accordance with what reason requires. (Then) it indicates (either metaphorically, or by placement as shared or independent, and the first two) – indication metaphorically and by sharing – are contrary to the principle, and one resorts to them only with evidence, and there is none. (Thus) the aforementioned answer is refuted in both aspects: first, because metaphor and sharing are contrary to principle; second, because it is not pure opinion but induction has a role in it, like the objection with 'kull' and 'jami'. (And similarly) just as the objection that one can dispense in expressing generality with the word 'kull' and 'jami', which are outside the dispute, so placement for other words is not required due to lack of need, is refuted. The point of refutation is that we have found the mentioned formulas indicating generality, but there remains something: it suffices that induction indicates that the mentioned formulas indicate generality, whether metaphorically, or by sharing, or independently, and the first two are contrary to principle, and there is no need for it to be a meaning needing expression, so there is redundancy in the argument, so reflect. Those who said the formulas are literal for specificity and metaphorical for generality (said) in the argument (first): There is no generality except in a compound, and the single word is for other than generality, because the meaning of condition, inclusion of the article, etc., of the annex, indefinite in negation, and relative pronouns (are not realized except by joining another word) with it, so they have no generality. (The answer is that suspense regarding indication of the compound with others does not necessitate that the totality is the indicator; rather, it is possible that the indicator is the single word, but in the state of composition. So we do not concede that there is no generality except in a compound; its utmost is that the placement for generality is generic, within a universal rule, such that the assignor specifies the indefinite in the context of negation for inclusiveness, and similarly the placements of derived words, dual, plural, diminutive, and the like. (And) they said (second): Specificity is certain and generality is doubtful, and what is certain is more deserving than the doubtful. So the specific is more deserving. We say: The doubtful is made certain by the evidence that has passed, and that specificity is certain is denied; rather, its absence is certain. (Moreover, it is establishing language and placement by preference and opinion, which is invalid. On the contrary, working by generality is more precautionary and comprehensive, because by acting on generality the obligated person is discharged from responsibility with certainty, so precaution contradicts the certainty of specificity. It is said: Precaution is not universal, for it is only in obligation and prohibition, not permissibility, and that does not harm us, because the purpose is to refute the proof that what is certain does not benefit you, as it is opposed by precaution, even if in some cases, so reflect. (And) they said (third): It is famous that there is no general except that some of it has been specified, and this general has been specified by something like His saying, 'And Allah is Knowing of all things' until it became proverbial. So generality is defeated and specificity is prevalent, and what is defeated is metaphorical, so generality is metaphorical. In his saying 'wa qad lama khuss' is a refutation of the suspicion that this proposition invalidates itself because it also contains generality. The point of refutation is that this general is specified, so it is not invalid. We say: This is for us, not against us. And specification by evidence is a branch of generality in terms of placement, so this confirms the placement. (Hence it remains general after specification in what remains). Moreover, that the defeated is absolutely metaphorical is denied, and that the less frequently used may be necessitated by evidence requiring it, and here the evidence indicates generality. As for those who say it is shared and those who suspend judgment (they said): Each of them is used for both generality and specificity, and the principle in usage is literalness in both, so sharing is necessitated. Or it is said: It is used for each, and one does not know which it is placed for, so suspension is necessary. From here – meaning due to sharing or suspension regarding placement – they went to the view that the general is ambiguous and must be suspended until clarification comes. We say: That the principle is literalness in both and the lack of knowledge of placement is denied. Rather, the evidence stands that they are placed for generality, and sharing is contrary to principle. Those who say there is generality in commands and prohibitions (they said): Obligation is for everyone, and it is by command and prohibition, so they are for generality, unlike reports. We say: The utmost that follows is their usage for generality, but placement is denied and not necessitated. Rather, it is permissible that the indication be by context as before. But, what is necessary from what we mentioned is the placement, but absolutely for command, prohibition, or report. Indeed, the intended report may be about everything, just as obligation is for everyone. And it is only through the report with generality and its form. And knowledge (i.e., belief in the mentioned report) is required by the Lawgiver like actions, so generality follows in the report as well, with the same reasoning you mentioned. It is said: If the argument were valid, it would necessitate the generality of 'pray' and 'fast', but the generality of 'pray' and 'fast' is not the subject of dispute, for no one said that command and prohibition are for generality. (I say: His meaning is that those formulas are general when used in injunctive speech, not that the injunctive speech itself is general. For example, 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' (Quran 2:185), the conditional word in it is general. (So reflect). But the conclusion of their doctrine then is that examples like 'man' and other formulas in requests are...
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is an extended argument from the commentary (sharh) defending the position that general words ('umum) are independently placed for the meaning of generality, not derived from other meanings through metaphor or shared usage. The author first presents the rational proof: the frequent need to express the concept of generality necessitates that the assignor of language (al-wadi') must have established specific words for it, just as with other intended meanings. He then refutes the objection that this need can be met by using words metaphorically or as homonyms: such usage is contrary to the original principle (al-asl) in language, which prefers literal independent placement. Moreover, the claim that this argument relies on mere opinion (ra'y) is invalid because the proof is based on induction (istiqra') from actual usage. The author then addresses three specific objections. First, those who say generality only occurs in compound expressions (e.g., 'every man' requires 'man' + 'every'): the answer is that the independent word can still indicate generality when in composition, and the placement is generic (naw'i) under a universal rule, just like derived words and plural forms. Second, those who say specificity is certain while generality is doubtful: the author denies the certainty of specificity, citing the evidence for generality, and notes that acting on generality is precautionary (ihtiyat) for discharging obligation, which outweighs mere certainty. Third, those who say all generals have been specified, making generality metaphorical: the author argues that specification is a branch of generality in terms of placement, and an exception does not negate the rule; further, the prevalence of specification does not make generality metaphorical. The author then addresses those who hold that 'amm is a homonym (ishtirak) or that one must suspend judgment (tawaqquf): he rejects homonymy because it is contrary to principle, and evidence establishes the independent placement. Finally, he examines the claim that generality only applies to commands and prohibitions, not reports: the author argues that reports can also intend universal meaning (like knowledge of a ruling), and the example of 'man' in the condition 'faman shahida...' shows the general formula in an injunctive context. Throughout the passage, the author systematically refutes each opposing view, reaffirming the Hanafi usul position that general words are independently placed for generality.

Key Terms
العموم (al-'umum): The meaning of generality or inclusiveness intended to be conveyed by a word or phrase.
الخصوص (al-khusus): The meaning of specificity, as opposed to generality.
المجاز (al-majaz): Metaphorical usage, where a word is used for a meaning other than its original literal meaning.
الاشتراك (al-ishtirak): A word having multiple meanings (homonymy), e.g., 'ayn for eye, spring, etc.
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment regarding the meaning of a word until evidence clarifies it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main refutation of the objection that metaphor or homonymy can express generality without independent placement?
A) Metaphor and homonymy are impossible in Arabic.
B) Metaphor and homonymy are contrary to the original principle (asl) and required evidence, which is absent.
C) The Quran forbids metaphor.
D) Homonymy always leads to confusion.

Key Takeaway
General words are independently placed for generality based on rational necessity and inductive evidence, making them definitive in their scope.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Refuting Objections Against Independent Placement of General Words
Refutation of five specific objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and refute the five main objections against the Hanafi position that general words are independently placed for generality.

Core Idea
The five objections (compound, certainty, specification, homonymy, restriction to injunctions) are all refuted by Hanafi usul principles.

In this lesson, we continue the extended argument by examining the five specific objections that opponents raise against the independent placement of general words. These objections come from different groups: those who restrict generality to compounds, those who argue specificity is certain, those who claim all generals are specified, those who say 'amm is a homonym or ambiguous, and those who limit generality to commands and prohibitions. The author provides clear Hanafi responses to each, confirming the strength of the original position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Five Objections
The passage lists five groups of opponents: (1) those saying generality only in compounds, (2) those saying specificity is certain, (3) those saying all generals are specified so metaphor, (4) those saying homonymy or suspension, (5) those limiting to commands/prohibitions.
2
Analyze the First Objection (Compound)
Opponents argue that words like 'man' (who), 'kull' (every), and constructs like conditionals only indicate generality in compound phrases. The Hanafi response: the single word can still indicate generality when in composition; placement is generic (naw'i) under a universal rule.
The example of 'man' in 'faman shahida' shows a single word with general meaning.
3
Analyze the Second Objection (Certainty of Specificity)
Opponents say specificity is certain while generality is doubtful. Hanafi response: specificity is not certain; evidence supports generality, and acting on generality is precautionary (ihtiyat), which outweighs mere claimed certainty.
4
Analyze the Third Objection (Prevalence of Specification)
Opponents note that every general has been specified, so generality is metaphorical. Hanafi response: specification presupposes generality (takhsis far' of 'umum), and the fact that specification occurs does not make the original placement metaphorical; the remnant remains general.
The verse 'Allah is Knowing of all things' is cited as an example of a general that has been specified but still indicates generality.
5
Analyze the Fourth Objection (Homonymy/Suspension)
Opponents say words like 'every' are used for both generality and specificity, so they are homonyms or require suspension. Hanafi response: evidence shows they are placed for generality; homonymy is contrary to principle.
6
Analyze the Fifth Objection (Commands/Prohibitions Only)
Opponents restrict generality to commands and prohibitions. Hanafi response: reports can also convey generality, because knowledge (i'tiqad) is required by the Lawgiver, and general reports achieve that. The example of 'man' in a conditional shows a general formula in an injunctive context.
The author clarifies that the dispute is about the scope of general formulas, not about command and prohibition themselves.

(He argued) for the chosen position (that) it is a meaning intended to be conveyed, and the need to express it is frequent, so it must have been placed for it like other meanings for which words were placed to express them. It was answered that one can dispense, in expressing it, with independent placement (through metaphor and shared word); it is permissible for words to be for specificity and used for generality metaphorically, or to be shared between generality and specificity, then used for generality, so the need for expression is fulfilled and independent placement is not required. (And) it was answered that this is establishing language and placement by opinion and analogy, which has been prohibited. (I say: If it were said in the argument that generality is a rational meaning, the need to express it is frequent, then indication of it is necessary, i.e., there must be some word indicating it, rather many words, otherwise it would be impossible to express and convey generality, and indication has been found through induction in words in accordance with what reason requires. (Then) it indicates (either metaphorically, or by placement as shared or independent, and the first two) – indication metaphorically and by sharing – are contrary to the principle, and one resorts to them only with evidence, and there is none. (Thus) the aforementioned answer is refuted in both aspects: first, because metaphor and sharing are contrary to principle; second, because it is not pure opinion but induction has a role in it, like the objection with 'kull' and 'jami'. (And similarly) just as the objection that one can dispense in expressing generality with the word 'kull' and 'jami', which are outside the dispute, so placement for other words is not required due to lack of need, is refuted. The point of refutation is that we have found the mentioned formulas indicating generality, but there remains something: it suffices that induction indicates that the mentioned formulas indicate generality, whether metaphorically, or by sharing, or independently, and the first two are contrary to principle, and there is no need for it to be a meaning needing expression, so there is redundancy in the argument, so reflect. Those who said the formulas are literal for specificity and metaphorical for generality (said) in the argument (first): There is no generality except in a compound, and the single word is for other than generality, because the meaning of condition, inclusion of the article, etc., of the annex, indefinite in negation, and relative pronouns (are not realized except by joining another word) with it, so they have no generality. (The answer is that suspense regarding indication of the compound with others does not necessitate that the totality is the indicator; rather, it is possible that the indicator is the single word, but in the state of composition. So we do not concede that there is no generality except in a compound; its utmost is that the placement for generality is generic, within a universal rule, such that the assignor specifies the indefinite in the context of negation for inclusiveness, and similarly the placements of derived words, dual, plural, diminutive, and the like. (And) they said (second): Specificity is certain and generality is doubtful, and what is certain is more deserving than the doubtful. So the specific is more deserving. We say: The doubtful is made certain by the evidence that has passed, and that specificity is certain is denied; rather, its absence is certain. (Moreover, it is establishing language and placement by preference and opinion, which is invalid. On the contrary, working by generality is more precautionary and comprehensive, because by acting on generality the obligated person is discharged from responsibility with certainty, so precaution contradicts the certainty of specificity. It is said: Precaution is not universal, for it is only in obligation and prohibition, not permissibility, and that does not harm us, because the purpose is to refute the proof that what is certain does not benefit you, as it is opposed by precaution, even if in some cases, so reflect. (And) they said (third): It is famous that there is no general except that some of it has been specified, and this general has been specified by something like His saying, 'And Allah is Knowing of all things' until it became proverbial. So generality is defeated and specificity is prevalent, and what is defeated is metaphorical, so generality is metaphorical. In his saying 'wa qad lama khuss' is a refutation of the suspicion that this proposition invalidates itself because it also contains generality. The point of refutation is that this general is specified, so it is not invalid. We say: This is for us, not against us. And specification by evidence is a branch of generality in terms of placement, so this confirms the placement. (Hence it remains general after specification in what remains). Moreover, that the defeated is absolutely metaphorical is denied, and that the less frequently used may be necessitated by evidence requiring it, and here the evidence indicates generality. As for those who say it is shared and those who suspend judgment (they said): Each of them is used for both generality and specificity, and the principle in usage is literalness in both, so sharing is necessitated. Or it is said: It is used for each, and one does not know which it is placed for, so suspension is necessary. From here – meaning due to sharing or suspension regarding placement – they went to the view that the general is ambiguous and must be suspended until clarification comes. We say: That the principle is literalness in both and the lack of knowledge of placement is denied. Rather, the evidence stands that they are placed for generality, and sharing is contrary to principle. Those who say there is generality in commands and prohibitions (they said): Obligation is for everyone, and it is by command and prohibition, so they are for generality, unlike reports. We say: The utmost that follows is their usage for generality, but placement is denied and not necessitated. Rather, it is permissible that the indication be by context as before. But, what is necessary from what we mentioned is the placement, but absolutely for command, prohibition, or report. Indeed, the intended report may be about everything, just as obligation is for everyone. And it is only through the report with generality and its form. And knowledge (i.e., belief in the mentioned report) is required by the Lawgiver like actions, so generality follows in the report as well, with the same reasoning you mentioned. It is said: If the argument were valid, it would necessitate the generality of 'pray' and 'fast', but the generality of 'pray' and 'fast' is not the subject of dispute, for no one said that command and prohibition are for generality. (I say: His meaning is that those formulas are general when used in injunctive speech, not that the injunctive speech itself is general. For example, 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' (Quran 2:185), the conditional word in it is general. (So reflect). But the conclusion of their doctrine then is that examples like 'man' and other formulas in requests are...
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is an extended argument from the commentary (sharh) defending the position that general words ('umum) are independently placed for the meaning of generality, not derived from other meanings through metaphor or shared usage. The author first presents the rational proof: the frequent need to express the concept of generality necessitates that the assignor of language (al-wadi') must have established specific words for it, just as with other intended meanings. He then refutes the objection that this need can be met by using words metaphorically or as homonyms: such usage is contrary to the original principle (al-asl) in language, which prefers literal independent placement. Moreover, the claim that this argument relies on mere opinion (ra'y) is invalid because the proof is based on induction (istiqra') from actual usage. The author then addresses three specific objections. First, those who say generality only occurs in compound expressions (e.g., 'every man' requires 'man' + 'every'): the answer is that the independent word can still indicate generality when in composition, and the placement is generic (naw'i) under a universal rule, just like derived words and plural forms. Second, those who say specificity is certain while generality is doubtful: the author denies the certainty of specificity, citing the evidence for generality, and notes that acting on generality is precautionary (ihtiyat) for discharging obligation, which outweighs mere certainty. Third, those who say all generals have been specified, making generality metaphorical: the author argues that specification is a branch of generality in terms of placement, and an exception does not negate the rule; further, the prevalence of specification does not make generality metaphorical. The author then addresses those who hold that 'amm is a homonym (ishtirak) or that one must suspend judgment (tawaqquf): he rejects homonymy because it is contrary to principle, and evidence establishes the independent placement. Finally, he examines the claim that generality only applies to commands and prohibitions, not reports: the author argues that reports can also intend universal meaning (like knowledge of a ruling), and the example of 'man' in the condition 'faman shahida...' shows the general formula in an injunctive context. Throughout the passage, the author systematically refutes each opposing view, reaffirming the Hanafi usul position that general words are independently placed for generality.

Key Terms
العموم (al-'umum): The meaning of generality.
الخصوص (al-khusus): The meaning of specificity.
المجاز (al-majaz): Metaphor.
الاشتراك (al-ishtirak): Homonymy.
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment.
النوعي (al-naw'i): Generic placement under a universal rule.
الأحوط (al-ahwat): The more precautionary (opinion).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) They admit that generality is metaphorical because specification is common.
B) They argue that specification confirms the placement of generality, and the remnant remains general.
C) They deny that any general has been specified.
D) They say that specification only applies to commands.

Key Takeaway
The five objections are systematically refuted, confirming that general words are independently placed for generality.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Three Objections to Generality Refuted
Refutation of three objections to generality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three objections against generality and apply the Hanafi response that evidence establishes designation for generality.

Core Idea
General terms are designated for generality; specification confirms, not negates, the original wad‘.

The passage begins by refuting arguments that general terms are not truly general. Three objections are raised: that particularity is certain, that specification is pervasive, and that composition negates individual word generality. The Hanafi response is that evidence establishes generality, specification is a branch of generality, and the argument from composition is irrelevant. This lesson unpacks each objection and the rebuttals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three objections
Locate the three arguments against generality: (1) particularity is certain, (2) specification is common making generality overcome, (3) generality requires compound. Understand each claim.
The objections appear after 'قالوا ثانياً' and 'قالوا ثالثاً' and the initial point about composition.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to each
For each objection, the author gives a counterargument. Summarize how the Hanafi position refutes each one: evidence establishes generality, specification confirms the original wad‘, and composition argument is denied.
Note the use of 'قلنا' as the response marker.
3
Extract the Hanafi principle
From the responses, derive the Hanafi usul principle: العموم وضع للعموم unless there is قرينة, and التخصيص فرع الوضع.
This principle governs how Hanafis treat general texts without specification.

المقالة الثالثة في المبادىء اللغوية الدلالة على التركيب) مع غيره (لا يستلزم أن المجموع هو الدال بل يجوز أن يكون الدال هو المفرد، لكن حال التركيب فلا نسلم أن لا عموم إلا لمركب وغايته أن الوضع) للعموم (نوعي) في ضمن قاعدة كلية بأن يعين الواضع النكرة الواقعة تحت النفي للاستغراق وهكذا كأوضاع المشتقات والمثنى والجمع والمصغر وأمثالها (و) قالوا (ثانياً : إن الخصوص متيقن) والعموم مشكوك (وهو) أي المتيقن أولى من (المشكوك فالمخصوص أولى قلنا: المشكوك متيقن بالدليل الذي مر وكون الخصوص متيقناً ممنوع، بل عدمه متيقن (مع أنه إثبات اللغة) والوضع (بالترجيح) والرأي فلا يصح على أن العموم أحوط وأجمع) فإنه بالعمل بالعموم يخرج المكلف عن العهدة بيقين فتعارض الأحوطية تيقن الخصوص، قيل: الأحوطية لا يطرد فإنه إنما يكون في الوجوب والتحريم دون الإباحة ولا يضرنا، فإن المقصود نقض الدليل بأن المتيقن لا يفيدكم فإنه معارض بالأحوطية ولو في بعض الموارد فتأمل (و) قالوا (ثالثاً) قد اشتهر ما من عام إلا وقد خص منه البعض وقد خص)، هذا العام (بنحو) قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاللَّهُ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۸۲] [النساء : ١٧٦] [النور: ٣٥ - ٦٤] حتى صار مثلاً، فالعموم مغلوب والخصوص غالب والمغلوب هو المجاز) فالعموم مجاز وفي قوله : وقد لما خص دفع يتوهم التشكيك بأن هذه القضية مبطلة لنفسها فإنها أيضاً مشتملة على العموم، وجه الدفع أن هذا العام ،مخصوص، فلا يبطل (قلنا) هذا لنا لا علينا (والتخصيص لدليل فرع العموم وضعاً فهذا مثبت للوضع (ولهذا يعم) بعد التخصيص (فيما بقي على أن) كون المغلوب مجازاً مطلقاً ممنوع ، وأن الأقل قد يلزم لدليل موجب إياه، وههنا دل الدليل على العموم، هذا القائلون بالاشتراك والمتوقفون (قالوا : أطلقت كل منها للعموم والخصوص) جميعاً (والأصل) في الإطلاق (الحقيقة) فيهما) فيلزم الاشتراك (أو) يقال : أطلقت لكل منهما ولا يدري) الوضع لأيهما فيجب التوقف ومن ههنا أي من أجل الاشتراك أو التوقف في الوضع ذهبوا إلى أن العام مجمل يجب فيه التوقف حتى يرد البيان (قلنا) كون الأصل حقيقة فيهما وعدم دراية الوضع (ممنوع) بل الدليل قام على أنها موضوعة للعموم، والاشتراك خلاف الأصل، قائلو العموم في الأمر والنهي (قالوا: التكليف للكل وهو بالأمر والنهي، فهما للعموم بخلاف الأخبار (قلنا) غاية ما لزم الاستعمال فيهما للعموم والوضع ممنوع) وغير لازم منه (بل) يجوز أن تكون الدلالة (بالقرينة كما تقدم نعم : يلزم مما ذكرنا الوضع، لكن مطلقاً أمراً أو نهياً أو إخباراً على أن (الإخبار المقصود قد يكون عن الكل كالتكليف يكون للكل (وهو) إنما يكون (بالخبر به أي بالعموم وصيغته والمعرفة). أي الاعتقاد بالخبر المذكور (مطلوبة) للشارع كالأعمال فيلزم العموم في الخبر أيضاً بعين ما قلتم هذا (قيل) لو تم الاستدلال يلزم عموم صلوا وصوموا) و (عموم) صلوا وصوموا غير محل النزاع) فإن أحداً لم يقل الأمر والنهي للعموم (أقول : مراده أن تلك الصيغ تعم إذا استعملت في الإنشاء) لا أن الإنشاء نفسه يعم (نحو : ﴿فَمَن شَهِدَ مِنكُمُ الشَّهْرَ فَلْيَصُمْهُ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٨٥] ) فكلمة الشرط الواقعة فيه تعم (فتأمل) لكن يكون حاصل مذهبهم حينئذ أن أمثال من وغيرها من الصيغ في الطلب أن صيغ موضوعة للعموم وفي الإخبار ليست موضوعة له وهو كما ترى فافهم .
The Third Article on Linguistic Principles: The indication of composition) with others (does not necessitate that the whole is the indicator; rather it is possible that the individual word is the indicator, but in the state of composition. So we do not concede that there is no generality except in a compound. Its utmost is that the designation) for generality (is generic) within a universal rule, as the positer specifies the indefinite noun occurring under negation for totality, and similarly for derivations, duals, plurals, diminutives, and the like. (And) they said (secondly: Particularity is certain) and generality is doubtful (and it) i.e., the certain (is more deserving than) the doubtful (so the particular is more deserving. We said: The doubtful is made certain by the evidence that passed, and that particularity is certain is denied; rather its absence is certain. (Moreover, it is establishing the language) and the designation (by preference) and opinion, so it is invalid. But generality is more precautionary and comprehensive) for by acting on generality the responsible person is absolved with certainty. So precaution conflicts with the certainty of particularity. It was said: Precaution is not universal, for it is only in obligation and prohibition, not permission, but that does not harm us, for the purpose is to refute the evidence that the certain does not benefit you, for it is opposed by precaution even in some cases, so reflect. (And) they said (thirdly): It is well-known that there is no general but that some part of it has been specified, and this general has been specified) by something like His statement: {And Allah is Knower of all things} [2:282, 4:176, 24:35-64] until it became proverbial. So generality is overcome and particularity prevails, and the overcome is metaphorical) so generality is metaphorical. In his saying 'and it has been specified' there is a daf' of the suspicion that this proposition refutes itself because it also contains generality. The daf': This general is specified, so it is not invalid. (We said): This is for us, not against us. (And specification by evidence is a branch of generality in terms of designation, so this confirms the designation. (And therefore it applies generally) after specification (in what remains, besides that) the fact that the overcome is absolutely metaphorical is denied, and that the lesser may be necessitated by evidence necessitating it, and here evidence has indicated generality. These are the proponents of commonality (ishtirak) and suspension (tawaqquf). (They said: Each was used for generality and particularity) together (and the principle) in usage (is the real meaning) in both) so commonality is necessitated. (Or) it is said: It was used for each but it is not known) which designation is intended, so suspension is obligatory. From here, i.e., because of commonality or suspension in designation, they opine that the general is ambiguous (mujmal) requiring suspension until clarification comes. (We said): That the principle is the real meaning in both and lack of knowledge of designation (is denied); rather evidence has established that they are designated for generality, and commonality is contrary to the principle. Proponents of generality in command and prohibition (said: The obligation is for all, and it is by command and prohibition, so these two are for generality unlike reports. (We said): The utmost necessitated is usage in them for generality, while designation is denied) and not necessitated from it; (rather) it is possible that the indication is (by context as before. Yes, what we mentioned necessitates designation, but absolutely, whether command, prohibition, or report. (Moreover, the report intended may be about the whole, like obligation is for all, (and it) is only (by the report of it, i.e., by generality and its form and knowledge). i.e., belief in the mentioned report (is required) by the Lawgiver like actions, so generality is necessitated in the report as well by the same argument you mentioned. This (was said): If your inference were valid, it would necessitate the generality of 'pray' and 'fast' (and) the generality of 'pray' and 'fast' is not the point of dispute) for no one says command and prohibition are for generality. (I say: He intends that those forms are general when used in construction) not that construction itself is general. (Like: {So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it} [2:185]) so the conditional particle in it is general. (So reflect) but then the gist of their doctrine is that like 'man' and other forms in requests are designated for generality, while in reports they are not designated for it, and that is as you see, so understand.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
The passage presents a usul dispute about whether general terms are set for generality or involve commonality/suspension. The author first refutes the claim that particularity is certain by arguing that the evidence establishes generality. He then addresses the argument that generality is overcome by specification, noting that specification itself relies on the original designation of generality. The proponents of ishtirak (commonality) and tawaqquf (suspension) argue that terms are used for both generality and particularity, necessitating ambiguity. The Hanafi response is that the principle is real meaning for each, and the evidence shows designation for generality; commonality is contrary to the principle. A further argument from command/prohibition is that obligation applies to all, so these forms are for generality. The author counters that usage does not prove designation; context may indicate generality. The section ends with a note that some distinguish between requests and reports, but the Hanafi position is that both are general based on the same reasoning.

Key Terms
العموم (al-ʿumūm): The quality of a word that designates all individuals of its referent without exception.
الاشتراك (al-ishtirāk): A single word having multiple meanings by designation.
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Suspending judgment on the meaning of a word until evidence clarifies it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response to the third objection (specification is common), what is the status of a general term after it has been specified?
A) It becomes metaphorical and loses its general meaning.
B) It remains general in what remains, because specification is a branch of generality.
C) It becomes particular in all cases.
D) It becomes ambiguous and requires further clarification.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul holds that general terms are designated for generality and remain general after specification in the unspecified remainder.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Case for Ishtirak and Tawaqquf Refuted; Generality in Commands and Reports
Refutation of ishtirak/tawaqquf and defense of generality in commands and reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the argument that commands are general but reports are not, and state the Hanafi position that both are general based on consistent reasoning.

Core Idea
Commands and reports both require generality; the Lawgiver's address to all necessitates generality in both obligations and information.

This lesson continues the debate on generality, focusing on the claim that general terms involve ishtirak (commonality) or require tawaqquf (suspension). The Hanafi response is that evidence establishes designation for generality. Then the discussion turns to whether commands and prohibitions are general but reports are not. The author refutes this distinction, arguing that both are general by the same reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's position on ishtirak/tawaqquf
The opponents argue that terms are used for both generality and particularity, leading to ishtirak; or that it is unknown which meaning is intended, leading to tawaqquf. Understand their reasoning.
Look for 'الاشتراك والمتوقفون قالوا'
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to ishtirak/tawaqquf
The Hanafi response denies that the principle is real in both meanings. Evidence establishes that the word is designated for generality, and ishtirak is contrary to the principle of language.
The marker 'قلنا' appears.
3
Examine the argument from command/prohibition
Opponents claim that commands and prohibitions are for generality, but reports are not. The Hanafi rebuttal is that the same evidence applies to reports: obligation (taklif) is for all, and similarly knowledge from reports is required for all.
Note the phrase 'التكليف للكل' and how it is extended to reports.
4
Evaluate the final distinction and its limitations
The author mentions a view that distinguishes between requests (constructive) and reports, but ultimately dismisses it, affirming that both are general when used in the appropriate form.
See the end where it says 'فافهم'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How does the Hanafi response refute the argument that reports are not general?
A) By saying that reports are not part of sharia.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

The General Term is Definitive in Hanafi Usul
Ruling that general terms are definitive and cannot be specified by weak evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that general terms (عام) are definitive (قطعي) in the sense of not admitting ordinary probability, and apply it to determine why a general Quranic verse cannot be specified by a solitary hadith or analogy.

Core Idea
A general term alone is definitive; weak evidence like solitary hadith cannot overturn it.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut ala Muslim al-Thubut explains the Hanafi doctrine that general terms (عام) are definitive (قطعي) in their indication of generality. The author first distinguishes two meanings of 'definitive' and establishes that the general is definitive in the second sense—meaning no ordinary probability but rationally possible. The practical consequence is that a general Quranic verse cannot be specified by a solitary hadith (خبر الواحد) or analogy (قياس). The passage also addresses the opposing view (mainly Shafi'i, Maliki, and some Hanafis like al-Maturidi) and responds to the objection based on the frequency of specification.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two meanings of 'definitive' (قطعي)
Identify the two possible meanings: (1) that which reason cannot oppose at all, and (2) that which does not admit opposition in customary speech but may be opposed rationally. Which one is intended for the general term?
The passage states the second meaning is intended.
2
Extract the Hanafi rule on specification
From the definition, derive the rule: the general term indicates generality definitively, so it cannot be specified by probabilistically established evidence like solitary hadith (ظني الثبوت) or analogy (ظني الدلالة).
This is the core ruling.
3
Identify the opposing view and its proof
The majority of Shafi'is and Malikis, and some Hanafis (e.g., al-Maturidi), hold that general terms are probabilistic (ظني) and can be specified by such evidence. Their proof is the frequency of specification (كثرة التخصيص) observed in the language.
Understand the source of disagreement.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the objection
The Hanafi response: frequency of specification does not create probability in the isolated general because each specification occurs with a specific context (قرينة صارفة). The general without context remains definitive. The frequency is not a context because it is not a single common usage that overrides the original meaning.
This refutes the opposing argument.
5
Apply the rule to a concrete example
Take the Quranic verse ﴿وَلَا تَأْكُلُوا مِمَّا لَمْ يُذْكَرِ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ﴾ and the hadith 'المؤمن يذبح على اسم الله سمى أو لم يسم'. According to Hanafi usul, the hadith cannot specify the verse because the verse's general term is qat'i and the hadith is zanni.
This is the example given in the passage.

أنه موضوع للعموم قطعاً للدلائل القطعية التي مرت (فهو ) أي العموم (مدلول له وثابت به قطعاً) لأن اللفظ لا يحتمل غير الموضوع له كالخاص إلا بدليل صارف عنه وحينئذ لا نزاع في الخصوص اعترض عليه أن ثبوت المدلول للفظ قطعاً مطلقاً ممنوع وإنما يثبت لو لم يحتمل الانصراف عنه بدليل وههنا قد دل كثرة التخصيص حتى صار ما من عام إلا وقد خص منه البعض مثلاً على أن احتمال التخصيص قائم في كل عام، وإن أريد أن الدلالة على العموم لازمة قطعاً فلا كلام فيه إنما الكلام في الإرادة وليست لازمة قطعاً للكثرة المذكورة، والجواب عنه أن من ضرورات العربية أن اللفظ المجرد عن القرينة الصارفة الظاهرة يتبادر منه الموضوع له، ولا يحتمل غيره في العرف والمحاورة، ومن أراد منه غير الموضوع له ينسب إلى المكروه، وأما كثرة وقوع التخصيص بالأنواع المختلفة حسب اقتضاء القرائن الصارفة لا يورث الاحتمال في العام المجرد أصلاً، والكلام ههنا في العام المجرد عن القرائن، فلا مجال للاحتمال كالخاص فإن قلت : كثرة وقوع التخصيص قرينة على احتماله، قلنا: إنما تصح الكثرة قرينة، لو كانت بحيث يكون كثير الاستعمال في بعض معين بحيث يفهم مع عدم وهل هذا إلا كما يكون للفظ خاص معانٍ مجازية يستعمل
Issue: The general term (is definitive according to us. Know that 'definitive' may be used to mean that which does not admit of opposition at all and reason does not permit it even if weak. And it may be used to mean that which does not admit of opposition arising from evidence, although it admits of some possibility. Both meanings share that opposition does not occur to the mind at all, and the speakers of the language do not consider it possible. They differ in that if opposition were conceived, reason would not permit it at all in the first, while in the second it permits it rationally, and speakers of the language consider both not as probability, and it is not considered in ordinary speech at all. What is intended here is the second meaning. Thus the general, according to us, indicates generality and does not admit of particularity being considered a probability in ordinary speech; rather, the speakers attribute the one who proposes it to foolishness. This is like the specific itself. (So it is not permissible to specify it, if it occurs in the Book, by a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) because it is probabilistically established (zanni al-thubut), (nor by analogy) because it is probabilistically indicative (zanni al-dalalah). For this reason they did not permit specifying His statement: {And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned} [6:121] by his saying: 'The believer slaughters in the name of Allah, whether he mentioned it or not,' nor by analogy to the one who forgets. Al-ʿAyni said in Sharh al-Hidayah: The hadith goes like this: 'The believer slaughters in the name of Allah, whether he mentioned it or not, as long as he did not intentionally [omit].' (And the majority) of the Shafiʿis and Malikis and some of us like Imam ʿAlam al-Huda al-Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (may Allah sanctify his secret) hold that it is probabilistic (zanni), admitting of particularity correctly according to custom, arising from evidence. (So it is permissible to specify it, even if it is in the Book, by solitary report and analogy. For us, it is definitively designated for generality due to the definitive evidences that have passed. (Thus it) i.e., generality (is a denoted meaning of it, established by it definitively) because the word does not admit of other than its designated meaning like the specific unless there is evidence diverting from it. In that case there is no dispute about particularity. It was objected that the establishment of the denoted meaning for the word definitively absolutely is denied; it is only established if it does not admit of being diverted from by evidence. Here the frequency of specification, to the point that there is no general but has been specified from it some part, for example, indicates that the possibility of specification exists in every general. And if it is meant that the indication of generality is necessary definitively, then there is no dispute; rather the dispute is about the intent, which is not necessarily definitive due to the mentioned frequency. The response to this is that it is a necessary of Arabic that a word devoid of a clear diverting context (qarina sarifa) immediately conveys its designated meaning, and does not admit of other in custom and ordinary speech. Whoever intends other than its designated meaning is attributed to the disliked. As for the frequency of specification occurring in various types due to the requirements of diverting contexts, it does not generate probability in the isolated general at all. The discussion here is about the general isolated from contexts, so there is no room for probability, like the specific. If you say: The frequency of specification is a context indicating its probability, we say: Frequency can only be a context if it is such that the word is frequently used for a particular meaning so that it is understood even without a diverting context, as when the real meaning becomes abandoned or the metaphorical becomes customary. That is not the case here, for the frequency of specification in the general is only that in some uses it is intended with one context, and in others with another context, so this prevalence is not a context. Is this not like a specific word having metaphorical meanings?
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (مسألة) stating that in the Hanafi school, general terms are قَطْعِيّ (definitive) in the sense that they do not admit of specification based on weak evidence like solitary reports or analogy. The author distinguishes two meanings of 'definitive': one that absolutely cannot be opposed even rationally, and another that does not admit opposition in customary speech although rationally possible. The intended meaning here is the second. Thus a general term indicates generality without the ordinary possibility of particularity; proposing particularity without strong evidence is considered foolish. Consequently, a general verse in the Quran cannot be specified by a solitary hadith (which is probabilistically established) or by analogy (which is probabilistically indicative). The author cites the example of the verse forbidding eating meat not slaughtered with God's name, which cannot be specified by the reported hadith about a believer's slaughter. The majority of Shafi'is, Malikis, and some Hanafis (like al-Maturidi) disagree, holding that general terms are probabilistic and can be specified by such evidence. The Hanafi proof is that general terms are definitively designated for generality based on the definitive evidences previously mentioned, and the word does not admit other meanings without a diverting context. An objection is raised that the frequency of specification shows possibility. The response: frequency of specification does not create probability in the isolated general because each specification occurs with a specific context; the general without context remains definitive.

Key Terms
القطعي (al-qaṭʿī): That which does not admit of opposition in customary speech, even if rationally possible; the second meaning.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur; it is ظني الثبوت.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why can the general term in the verse 'وَلَا تَأْكُلُوا مِمَّا لَمْ يُذْكَرِ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ' not be specified by the hadith 'المؤمن يذبح على اسم الله'?
A) Because the hadith is weak in its chain.
B) Because the general term is definitive, and the hadith is probabilistically established.
C) Because the verse is abrogated.
D) Because the hadith contradicts a stronger evidence.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a general term without context is definitive and cannot be overridden by probabilistically established evidence like solitary reports or analogy.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
15 min
The General ('Amm) is Definitive in the Hanafi School
Debate on the definitive vs. probable nature of the general in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the general ('amm) is qat'i in indication, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf regarding specification by solitary hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, the general is definitive like the specific — specification requires a manifest context, not mere possibility.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents the heart of the Hanafi position on the definitive nature of the general ('amm). Unlike the Shafi'i and Maliki schools, which treat the general as probable (zanni) and open to specification by weak evidence, Hanafis insist that the general's indication of all its individuals is certain as long as no manifest context diverts it. The practical stakes are high: a general Quranic verse cannot be specified by a solitary hadith or analogy according to the Hanafi view, which preserves the binding force of revealed texts.

Guided Path
1
Define what 'qat'i' means in this context
The passage clarifies two meanings of qat'i: (1) what cannot be opposed by the intellect at all, and (2) what does not admit disagreement arising from evidence in discourse. Identify which meaning is intended. The intended meaning is the second, which allows mental possibility but treats the general as certain in customary discourse.
The second meaning is that people of discourse treat the general as giving all individuals, even if mental possibility exists.
2
Identify the Hanafi thesis on the general
State that according to Hanafis, the general indicates all its individuals definitively (qat'i). It does not admit specification without a manifest context (qarina). The author compares it to the specific (khass) which also does not admit metaphorical interpretation without a context.
3
Locate the proof and the counter-evidence
The Hanafi proof is the definitive placement of the general for generality (wad' qat'i). The opposing evidence is the frequent occurrence of specification; opponents argue that because most general terms have been specified in some contexts, they must be probable.
The passage mentions that the Hadith 'The believer slaughters in the name of Allah...' is used as an example of specification by a solitary report.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the frequency objection
The author rebuts that specification always occurs with a context (qarina). When the general is stripped of context, it retains its definitive generality. The frequency of specification does not make the general probable in isolation, just as frequent metaphorical use does not make the specific word probable.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: According to Hanafis, a general Quranic verse cannot be specified by a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) or by analogy (qiyas), because the general is qat'i and those evidences are zanni (probable). Opponents allow such specification, leading to different rulings in many legal issues.
Example: Qur'an 6:121 prohibits eating meat without tasmiyah; a solitary hadith allows omission. Hanafis follow the general prohibition; Shafi'is follow the specification.

المختار لو كان ظنياً لجاز إرادة البعض في العرف والمحاورة بلا دليل صارف لأن الكلام فيما لا صارف والو جاز إرادة البعض بلا دليل لارتفع الأمان عن اللغة والشرع ولزم التلبيس (وأجيب) بمنع الملازمة والظن يجب العمل به فلا يرتفع الأمان لأنه مفيد للظن، وهذا الجواب ليس بشيء فإن المقصود هو أنه لو اعتبر عرفاً ومحاورة احتمال إرادة البعض وهو غير الموضوع له ارتفع الأمان في كل لفظ عاماً كان أو خاصاً، لأن الكل سواسية في احتمال إرادة غير الموضوع له، فإن المانع عن احتمال الغير لم يكن إلا انتفاء القرينة ولم يمنع فلا يصدق بعقد وفسخ ووعد ووعيد وخبر وإنشاء وأتي استحالة فوق هذا؟ وليس مقصود المستدل ارتفاع الأمان بعدم صحة العمل حتى يجاب بأن العمل واجب بالظن، وقد سددنا طريق الهرب إلى غلبة وقوع التخصيص فتذكر الظانون (قالوا) في الاستدلال كل عام يحتمل التخصيص) حتماً لا ناشئاً دليل (فإنه شائع كثير حتى وقع المثل المذكور فسرى الاحتمال في كل عام عام (ولهذا يؤكد بكل وأجمعين ولولا الاحتمال لما احتيج إلى التأكيد قلنا :أولاً: إن الدليل جار في الخاص أيضاً، لأن الاستعارة شائعة كثيرة في الأشعار وكلام البلغاء حتى وقع المثل أن الشعر كذب، ويعيب الشعراء الفصحاء شعراً خالياً عنها، فيحتمل كل خاص خاص واقع في محاورات البلغاء التجوز، وكثرته دليل عليه فما هو جوابكم فهو جوابنا، وثانياً : أنه إن أرادوا بكثرة وقوع التخصيص كثرة وقوع تخصيص معين بحيث يتبادر من غير قرينة أو يلتفت إليه، كالمجاز المتعارف فلا نسلم كثرة الوقوع ، كيف ولو كان كذلك لوجب التخصيص لا أنه يحتمل فقط، وليس هذا أقل القليل فضلاً عن الكثرة، وإن أرادوا وقوع أنواع التخصيص بأنواع القرائن بحيث يكون العام في استعمال مخصوصاً ببعض أفراده وفي استعمال آخر ببعض آخر
Set for generality and in reports it is not set for it, and it is as you see, so understand. Issue: The general (amm) is definitive (qat'i) according to us. Know that qat'i may be used to mean what does not admit disagreement at all and the intellect cannot conceive it even if weak, and it may be used to mean what does not admit disagreement arising from evidence, although it admits some possibility. Both meanings share that disagreement does not occur to the mind at all, and the people of language do not consider it possible. They differ in that if disagreement were imagined, the intellect would not allow it in the first meaning at all, but allows it in the second as a mental possibility. The people of discourse consider both as no possibility and it is not considered in discourse at all. What is intended here is the second meaning. So the general according to us indicates generality and does not admit specification in discourse as a possibility; rather, the people of discourse attribute its proponent to foolishness, and this is exactly like the specific (khass). (So it is not permissible to specify it if it occurs in the Book with a solitary report (khabar wahid) because it is probabilistically established (zanni thubut), nor with analogy (qiyas) because it is probabilistically indicative (zanni dalala). That is why they did not permit specifying His statement: {And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned} [Al-An'am 6:121] by his statement: 'The believer slaughters in the name of Allah, whether he has mentioned the name or not,' nor by analogy with the forgetful person. Al-Aini said in Sharh al-Hidayah: The hadith is thus: 'The believer slaughters in the name of Allah whether he has mentioned the name or not, as long as he does not intentionally omit.' The majority of the Shafi'is and Malikis, and some of us like Imam Alam al-Huda Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (may Allah sanctify his secret), hold that it is probable (zanni), admitting specification by a valid customary possibility arising from evidence, so it is permissible to specify it, even if in the Book, with a solitary report and analogy. For us, it is definitively set for generality due to the definitive proofs that have passed, so generality is indicated and established definitively. The objection is raised: The proof of the meaning for the utterance being definitive in an absolute sense is denied; it is only established if it does not admit being turned away by evidence. Here, the frequency of specification—such that there is no general that has not been specified in some part—indicates that the possibility of specification exists in every general. If the intention is that the indication of generality is necessary definitively, there is no dispute; the dispute is about intention, and it is not definitively necessary because of the mentioned frequency. The answer is that it is a necessity of Arabic that the expression stripped of a manifest diverting context gives immediate understanding of its established meaning, and does not admit anything else in custom and discourse. Whoever intends other than its established meaning is attributed to something disliked. As for the frequency of specification in different types according to the requirements of diverting contexts, it does not generate possibility in the general stripped of context at all. The discussion here is about the general stripped of contexts, so there is no room for possibility, like the specific. If you say: The frequency of specification is evidence of its possibility, we say: The frequency is only valid as evidence if it is such that it is frequently used in a particular meaning such that it is understood even without a diverting context, as when the literal meaning becomes abandoned or the metaphorical becomes common. The matter here is not so, for the frequency of specification in the general is only that in one usage some part is intended due to a context, and in another usage another part due to another context. So this predominance is not a contextual evidence. And is this not like when a specific word has metaphorical meanings used in each with a context, and this frequency is not valid as evidence? Also we say: If frequency were evidence for specification, then it would not be correct to intend generality at all in any general, and this contradicts your view as well. So memorize this, for it is worthy of memorization. It is also objected that the general has two possibilities: the possibility of metaphor and the possibility of specification, so it is not like the specific, which has only the possibility of metaphor. Sadr al-Shari'ah answered that no attention is paid to the many or few possibilities as long as they do not arise from evidence, so the many possibilities in the general do not cause it to fall below the specific, because they are not counted in custom and discourse since they do not arise from evidence. And in Al-Tahrir it is answered that there is no possibility in a general used in discourse except for one metaphor, since two metaphors cannot be intended in one usage. So a word with one metaphor and a word with two metaphors are equal in possibility in usage. It is objected that the general used, like 'the thief' (al-sariq), may be used metaphorically for the grave-robber (al-nabash) and also specified to some of its individuals, so it has both possibilities contrary to the specific. And it is not far to say that here, i.e., in the general, there are two placements: one for its meaning as particular or generic, and another for generality as generic. So you see 'al-aswad al-rumah' is literal in generality but metaphorical with respect to intending the brave. So 'al-sariq' if theft means grave-robbing and the generality of its individuals is intended, it is literal in generality though metaphorical in its meaning. So the general, by virtue of its placement for generality, does not admit except one metaphor like the specific, so it does not produce in the general more than the weakness of the specific. So memorize it for it is subtle. (And it is argued) for the chosen view: If it were probable, then intending some (parts) would be permissible in custom and discourse without a diverting context, because the discussion is about what has no diverting context. And if intending some without evidence were permissible, then trust in language and law would be lost and confusion would be necessary. (And it is answered) by denying the implication, and probability necessitates action so trust is not lost because it yields probability. This answer is nothing, for the intended point is that if the possibility of intending some other than the established meaning were considered in custom and discourse, trust would be lost in every word, general or specific, because all are equal in the possibility of intending other than the established meaning. For the preventer against the possibility of other was nothing but the absence of a context, and it is not prevented. Then trust would not be given to contracts, dissolutions, promises, threats, reports, and constructions. Is there impossibility beyond this? And the arguer's intention is not the loss of trust due to the invalidity of action so that it is answered that action is obligatory by probability. And we have blocked the escape route to the predominance of specification, so remember the probabilistic (opponents). (They said) in the argument: Every general admits specification inevitably without arising from evidence, for it is widespread and frequent such that the mentioned proverb has occurred, so the possibility spreads in every general. And that is why it is emphasized by 'kull' and 'ajma'in; if there were no possibility, emphasis would not be needed. We say: First, the argument applies to the specific as well, because metaphor is widespread and frequent in poetry and the speech of eloquent people such that the proverb that poetry is lies has occurred, and eloquent poets criticize poetry devoid of metaphor. So every specific occurring in the speech of eloquent people admits metaphor, and its frequency is evidence for it. So whatever your answer is, it is our answer. Second, if they mean by the frequency of specification a specific frequent specification such that it is understood without a context or one pays attention to it, like common metaphor, then we do not admit the frequency; how so? If it were so, it would necessitate specification, not just possibility, and this is not even the least, let alone frequency. And if they mean the occurrence of types of specification by types of contexts such that the general in one usage is specified to some individuals and in another usage to other individuals, [then]...
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about the definitive nature of the general ('amm) in Hanafi thought. The author opens by clarifying the meaning of 'qat'i' (definitive) in this context: it does not mean absolute impossibility of opposition, but rather that the people of discourse treat the general's indication of all its individuals as certain, just like the specific. Thus, for Hanafis, a general term in the Quran cannot be specified by a solitary hadith (khabar wahid, which is zanni in transmission) or by analogy (qiyas, which is zanni in indication). The example given is the Quranic verse prohibiting eating meat over which Allah's name was not mentioned; a hadith says a believer slaughters in Allah's name whether he mentions it or not. Hanafis do not allow specifying the verse by that hadith because the hadith is zanni al-thubut (probable in transmission) and the verse's general indication is qat'i. The majority of Shafi'is and Malikis, and even some Hanafis like al-Maturidi, hold that the general is zanni and can be specified by such evidences. The author then presents the Hanafi proof: the general is definitively set for generality, as shown by earlier definitive proofs. An objection based on the frequent occurrence of specification is rebutted by arguing that such specification always comes with a context (qarina) and does not affect the general when stripped of context. Further objections and responses discuss the possibility of metaphor versus specification, and why the general remains qat'i. The passage ends with a dialectical argument: if the general were zanni, trust in language would break down, as any utterance could be intended for a non-literal meaning without a context.

Key Terms
العام (al-amm): A word that indicates all individuals of its category without restriction
قطعي (qat'i): In this passage: what does not admit opposition arising from a valid evidence in custom and discourse, even if mentally possible
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary report that does not reach the level of tawatur, thus zanni in transmission

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, can a general ayah from the Quran be specified by a solitary hadith (khabar wahid)?
A) Yes, because the general is zanni and the solitary hadith provides specification.
B) No, because the general is qat'i and the solitary hadith is zanni al-thubut.
C) Yes, because both are from revelation and must be harmonized.
D) No, because the solitary hadith is not a valid source of law.

Key Takeaway
For Hanafis, the general is qat'i al-dalala, so it cannot be specified by zanni evidence like khabar wahid or qiyas.

Acting upon General Texts Before Searching for a Specifier: The Hanafi Position
Arguing for permissibility of acting on 'amm before investigating mukhassis, refuting claimed consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits acting upon a general text ('amm) before searching for a mukhassis (specifier), and evaluate the counter-claim of consensus by citing Sahaba practice and scholarly disagreement.

Core Idea
A general text is binding immediately; a claimed consensus cannot override the practice of the Sahaba.

This lesson addresses a foundational usul al-fiqh question: when we encounter a general command in the Quran or Sunnah, must we pause and search for any potential specifier before acting? The Hanafi school answers no—the general is a proof in itself. We examine the evidence from Sahaba practice and refute a commonly claimed consensus to the contrary. Understanding this ruling is crucial for correctly applying Hanafi usul in deriving fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The disagreement centers on whether it is permissible to act upon a general text ('amm) before investigating (al-bahth) for a possible specifier (mukhassis). State the Hanafi position and the opposing claim clearly.
This is an usul dispute with practical consequences for fatwa.
2
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
The Hanafi school holds that acting on 'amm before searching is not only permissible but obligatory. Their primary evidence is the practice of the Sahaba—specifically Umar and Fatima—who acted on general texts without prior investigation. No Companion objected to this practice.
This is a dalil naqli (narrative proof) of 'amal al-Sahaba.
3
Analyze the opposing claim of consensus
Al-Ghazali and al-Amidi claimed that there is consensus (ijma') on the prohibition of acting before searching. Identify this claim and understand its basis.
Consensus is a strong argument, but its existence here is contested.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal
The author denies the consensus claim, citing scholars like Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini, Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi who recorded disagreement. The practice of the Sahaba and the silence of early generations further refute the claimed ijma'. This shows the importance of verifying historical claims of consensus.
The refutation uses both direct counter-evidence and the absence of transmitted objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
(يجوز العمل بالعام قبل البحث عن المخصص) واستقصاء تفتيشه عندنا (وعليه الصيرفي والبيضاوي والأرموي) ويلوح آثار رضا صاحب المحصول (ونقل) الإمام حجة الإسلام (الغزالي والآمدي الإجماع على المنع من العمل به قبل البحث عن المخصص (وهو) أي ثبوت الإجماع (ممنوع) والنقل غير مطابق ( فإن الأستاذ أبا إسحاق الإسفراييني وأبا إسحق الشيرازي والإمام فخر الدين الرازي (حكوا (الخلاف و به اندفع ما قال الشيخ ابن الهمام نقل الإجماع مبني على عدم اعتداد قول الصيرفي فإنه مكابرة بل الأستاذ حكى الاتفاق على التمسك به قبل البحث عن المخصص في حياته صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وأزواجه أجمعين (وسلم كما في التيسير) وأدل الدليل على أن نقل الإجماع غير مطابق أن أمير المؤمنين عمر رضي الله عنه حكم بالدية في الأصابع بمجرد العلم بكتاب عمرو بن حزم رضي الله عنه وترك القياس والرأي، ولم يبحث عن المخصص ولم يسأل عنه، وكذا سيدة النساء فاطمة الزهراء رضي عنها تمسكت بما ظنته عاماً في الميراث مع عدم البحث والسؤال عن المخصص، ثم ظهر المخصص ظهور الشمس على نصف النهار وبالجملة لم ينقل عن واحد من الصحابة قط التوقف في العام إلى البحث عن المخصص ولا إنكار واحد منهم في المناظرات على من تمسك بالعام قبل البحث عن المخصص، وكذا في القرن الثاني والثالث، والحنفية يوجبون العمل به قبل البحث، واستقر هذا المذهب إلى الآن فأين الإجماع، وقد تقدم النقل عن القاضي الإمام أبي زيد من أن التوقف مبتدع بعد القرن الثالث، وقال أن التوقف مبتدع بعد القرن الثالث، وقال هو أيضاً، وجملة الجواب أن العامي يلزمه العمل بعمومه كما وأما الفقيه فيلزمه أن يحتاط لنفسه، فيقف ساعة سمع الله لاستكشاف هذا الاحتمال بالنظر في الأشباه مع كونه حجة للعمل به إن عمل، لكن يقف
Issue: It is permissible to act upon the general before searching for the specifier and exhaustive investigation of it according to us. And upon this are al-Sayrafi, al-Baydawi, and al-Urmawi. And signs of approval appear from the author of al-Mahsul. Imam Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali and al-Amidi transmitted consensus upon the prohibition of acting upon it before searching for the specifier. But the establishment of consensus is denied, and the transmission is not accurate. For al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini, Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, and Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi narrated the disagreement. And with this, what Shaykh Ibn al-Humam said is refuted: that the transmission of consensus is based on not considering the statement of al-Sayrafi, for it is obstinacy. Rather, al-Ustadh narrated agreement on clinging to it before searching for the specifier in his lifetime – may God bless him and his family and his Companions and his wives all – as in al-Taysir. And the clearest proof that the transmission of consensus is not accurate is that the Commander of the Faithful, Umar - may God be pleased with him - ruled regarding the diyah for fingers merely by knowing the letter of Amr ibn Hazm - may God be pleased with him - and he left aside analogy and opinion, and he did not search for the specifier nor ask about it. Likewise, the Mistress of Women, Fatima al-Zahra' - may God be pleased with her - clung to what she thought was general regarding inheritance without searching and asking about the specifier. Then the specifier appeared like the sun at midday. In summary, it has never been transmitted from any of the Companions that they stopped regarding a general term until searching for the specifier, nor has any of them in debates disapproved of someone who clung to a general before searching for the specifier. Likewise in the second and third centuries. And the Hanafis make acting upon it obligatory before searching, and this school has settled until now. So where is the consensus? And the transmission from al-Qadi Imam Abu Zayd has already preceded that stopping is an innovation after the third century, and he said that stopping is an innovation after the third century, and he also said: The summary of the answer is that the layperson is obliged to act upon its generality, and as for the jurist, it is incumbent upon him to be cautious for himself, so he pauses for a moment - God heard - to discover this probability by examining similar cases, despite it being a proof for acting upon it if he acts, but he pauses.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that it is permissible, and even obligatory according to the Hanafis, to act upon a general text before searching for a mukhassis (specifier). The author aligns with scholars like al-Sayrafi, al-Baydawi, and al-Urmawi, noting apparent approval from the author of al-Mahsul. The claim of consensus by al-Ghazali and al-Amidi that it is prohibited is strongly denied. The author provides evidence from the transmission of disagreement by earlier scholars such as Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini, Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. Ibn al-Humam's suggestion that the consensus claim only disregards al-Sayrafi's view is dismissed as obstinacy. The strongest proof is the practice of the Sahaba: Umar ibn al-Khattab applied the general ruling on diyah for fingers from the letter of Amr ibn Hazm without searching for a specifier, and Fatima al-Zahra' held to a general understanding of inheritance laws without prior investigation. No Companion is reported to have paused or objected to such practice. This continued through the second and third centuries. The Hanafi school has consistently required acting upon the general before searching for a specifier. The author concludes that claims of consensus are false. Regarding the second part: a distinction is made between a layperson (ammi) who must act on the generality, and a jurist (faqih) who should pause briefly to consider possible specifications by examining similar cases, even though the general remains a proof for action. The text ends incomplete (but the ruling is clear).

Key Terms
المخصص (al-mukhassis): A proof (dalil) that specifies a general term to some of its individuals, removing the remaining from the ruling.
البحث (al-bahth): The process of searching and investigating for a potential mukhassis before acting upon a general text.
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the mujtahidun of the Ummah on a ruling. Here, the claim of consensus on prohibition is refuted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on acting upon a general text before searching for a mukhassis (specifier)?
A) Prohibited, because consensus forbids it
B) Permissible, based on the practice of the Sahaba
C) Permissible only for laypersons, not for jurists
D) Obligatory only after thorough search

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits and obligates acting on a general text immediately; claims of consensus to the contrary are refuted by Sahaba practice and recorded disagreement.

Acting on the General Before Search: The Hanafi Position and Its Evidence
Debating the permissibility of acting on general text before search

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on acting upon a general text before searching for a specifier and identify the key evidence from the Sahaba that supports it.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school permits acting upon a general text immediately, as proven by the practice of 'Umar and Fatima.

This passage addresses a foundational usul dispute: may a jurist apply a general textual ruling before investigating possible exceptions? The Hanafis answer yes, based on Sahaba practice and the definitive nature of general language. We will examine the arguments and the refutation of the claimed consensus against it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The issue is whether one may act upon a general text ('amm) before searching for a specifier (mukhassis). The Hanafi position is that it is permissible and obligatory.
The opposing view claims that action must be suspended until search.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi school holds that it is permissible (and even obligatory) to act upon the general before search, as the text is qat'i in indication.
The text says 'يجوز' and later 'يوجبون'.
3
Examine the Sahaba evidence
The author cites 'Umar's ruling on blood money using a general text without searching for a specifier, and Fatima's action on inheritance before the specifier appeared.
No Sahaba is reported to have paused or objected.
4
Analyze the refutation of consensus
Al-Ghazali and al-Amidi claimed ijma' on prohibition, but the author denies this, citing other scholars who recorded disagreement.
The strongest proof against the claimed consensus is Sahaba practice.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf is that Hanafis act immediately, while opponents pause to search for specifiers before acting.

سمع
الله
لاستكشاف هذا الاحتمال بالنظر في الأشباه مع كونه حجة للعمل به إن عمل، لكن يقف

٢٥٥
المقالة الثالثة في المبادىء اللغوية احتياطاً حتى لا يحتاج إلى نقض ما أمضاه بتبين الخلاف، لكن الكلام في موجب النص نفسه، أما الاحتياط فضرب معين يترك به الأصل إلا أن الترك به لا يجب حتماً، وهذا الكلام ناطق بجواز العمل قبل البحث، قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية : التفصيل الأحسن أن الصحابة يجوز لهم العمل به قبل البحث عن المخصص فإنه لا يحتمل الخفاء عليهم لو كان، وأما العامي الذي يحتمل الخفاء عليه فلا بد له من التوقف، وأما المجتهدون الذين هم ذوو حظ عظيم من العلم فهم في حكم الصحابة وهذا مخالف لما نقل عن القاضي الإمام، وقد مر أنه قد خفي على سيدة النساء رضي الله عنها المخصص القطعي لما ظنته عاماً وعملت قبل البحث عنه، ولا وجه للتوقف بعد قيام دليل شرعي موجب للحكم الإلهي إلا احتياطاً ساعة لمن له رتبة الاجتهاد والتأمل، ولعله لهذا قال بعده وفيه ما فيه لنا ما تقدم أنه قطعي) دلالة فيستفاد منه الحكم قطعاً (فلا يتوقف) بعد العلم بالحكم الإلهي الثابت قطعاً على عدم احتمال المعارض) احتمالاً غير معتد به (ك) ما لا يتوقف في سائر القواطع على عدم احتمال النسخ والتأويل وهذا ظاهر جداً، ثم هذا الدليل يتم على القول بالظنية أيضاً، فإنه يفيد ظن حكم إلهي ظناً قوياً، فيجب العمل به من غير توقف لأجل احتمال مرجوح للإجماع على العمل بالراجح، أعجبني قول الواقفين حيث جعلوا العام في حكم المجمل حتى أوجبوا التوقف إلى ظهور المراد بل جعلوه لغزاً وكيف ساغ لهم هذا القول مع حكمهم بوضع الصيغ للعموم انفراداً، وهل هذا إلا تهافت فتأمل، وأنصف المتوفقون (قالوا : عارض دلالته احتمال المخصص) ولا حجة الاحتمال المعارض (قلنا) العام قاطع ولا احتمال للتخصيص إلا عقلاً، كاحتمال المجاز في الخاص، والاحتمال عقلاً لا يعارض الدلالة وضعاً فلا ينافي الحجية (فافهم) ولو سلم ظني فاحتمال المخصص احتمال مرجوح، ، فلا يعارض العموم الوضعي الراجح، ولا توقف دون المعارضة فافهم ثم المانعون للعمل قبل البحث اختلفوا في قدر البحث عنه، والأكثر ومنهم ابن شريح قالوا: يجب البحث إلى الظن بعدمه لأن الاستقراء إنما يفيد الظن والبحث إنما يكون بالاستقراء (فشرط العادة بالقطع ممنوع بل إنما تقضي العادة بالظن ولو (قوياً كما في المحصول بكون الظن ضعيفاً (أقول : لو قالوا مظنون المجتهد مقطوع) لأن مظنونه واجب العمل قطعاً كما مر في المقدمة آل النزاع لفظياً) فإن من الوجدان بالاستقراء الشديد (كان العام) قطعياً كالخاص لاحتماله المجاز (احتمالاً مرجوحاً غير معتد به وغير ناشيء عن دليل (بالاتفاق) وههنا أيضاً عدم المخصص صار مرجوحاً غير معتد به لعدم دلالة الدليل عليه،
